RATING: 10
Firstly the problems:
- Bad rulebook
- you will lose first 2-3 games (maybe because of missunderstanding of rules and also in order to get all the rules into memory)
- if you finish it, it will last 1.5 h and certainly not 60 min as written on the box :(

Good things:
- it does not feel repetative as Space Hulk the card game sometimes feels (although a very good game; and a lot shorter; genestealers are more similar in effects and only differ in movement)as ghosts are very different from each other and have different effects so the deck of ghost cards and the red incarnation card give you a unique experience.
- it feels you have really achieved something if you win :D
- it really feels you are fighting to the eadge and to the last drop of your energy with the ghosts. The Taoists are cool and there are moments when you feel that on your turn your Taoist has acomplished the impossible. 

I have won 1 out of 4 games now

It is more practical and smooth in compariton to Death Angel.

RATING: 10
This comes as close as possible to what I consider top co-op: Many meaningful and equally difficult decisions, extreme challenging (but doable), also difficult for someone to "overlord" the other players strategies, due to the random nature of the dice. But best (and why it is the top scoring co-op on my list) - it does not take a few hours of buildup to get to the gist of it - the terror strikes from the get go! (Unlike BSG/Arkham and others)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Update 2010 01 24

This is now my favorite solo game. I have a decent win rate on nightmare level, and I enjoy the challenge the game continues to offer. That said, there is so much randomness to the setup that some games are definitely easier than others, but the re-playability that brings makes it a decent trade-off. Also, the relatively short playtime makes any oddball session not a big deal.

Update 2009 12 26:

I've now played half a dozen more times, and I am kicking up my rating substantially. I now win consistently at the initiate level and feel ready to tackle the tougher difficulties. Getting to know the various powers and making them work together is very important, and once you figure it out the game difficulty becomes much more manageable

This is a fantastic euro for solo play. It's a compelling puzzle with a huge amount of variability built in due to the variety of Taoist powers, the variety of the ghosts and the different Wu-Feng incarnations in each session. 

Great game.

Original comment:

This is a hard game to rate because it is so hard to beat. 

I've now played about half a dozen games and came close once or twice, but I've never won. As a solo game, it has the potential to be fantastic, because it's a challenging single player experience which has a real win condition (unlike other solo-friendly games that I own like Agricola, Steam w/single player maps or Race for the Galaxy) AND the playtime is a reasonable 30-45 minutes (unlike LOTR). I'm just hoping that the difficulty is the result of my inexperience... if it's simply a question of winning when things come out in a certain order (like solitaire), then I will lose interest quickly.

For now, lots to explore.

RATING: 7
A very interesting coop.  I like the use of individual powers and random board layout.  Felt very pressured, increasing threats, constant pressure to address them.  Plays rather smoothly.  Very tight game.

The game I played was a 4-player on the easiest difficulty.  Even then, we only barely won and that was with having 2 people sacrifice themselves for "the greater good."  I've heard harder difficulties may be nigh impossible.

I like this one, even over Pandemic!  GS has a nicer flow to it, more options, more complex decisions and more pressure.  It felt more fun.  I would definitely play GS again.

RATING: 8.5
[i]2017/05/15 - 4 plays 2-4 players - 1 victory[/i]

Great coop game, with a very fast setup and a great ~1 h play time. The game seems to me way more tactical than pandemic, which has more of a strategic element.

The use of dice also make it more random than Pandemic, and dice variability must be taken into account in order to win.

The disposition of the tiles, the variable Wu-fengs and the random appearance of Ghosts and player powers ensure a huge replayability.

The default game difficulty is way harder than Pandemic, but on par with Shadowrun:Crossfire. But I don't see that as a problem, as difficulty in coops is easy to tweak.

This is a great game to play on weekdays, since it plays quickly, is absorbing and brings out lots of tension. I clearly feel much better when I win at Ghost Stories than when I win at Pandemic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This is really a great game. I'm fond of coop games for the most part and this is one of the best. The tension is non-stop and every turn seems to be crucial. This is also one of the most difficult coop games to win that I've come across. But the level of tension and difficulty are only part of why I like the game so much. Unlike most other solitaire games I think Ghost Stories has a lot of player interaction. Sometimes a players best option is to devote their turn to just helping another player. All of the players seem to need to constantly be coming up with ways to help each other out. I also like it that the game comes with multiple levels of difficulty and that it takes some playing to figure out how to use all the tiles and powers to their fullest. There is much more variety here than in other coop games. It certainly gives the game some very good replayability. The game also plays fairly quickly. The 60 minutes listed on the box is about right. 

The game is also quite good solo. You can play with either a single taoist or play multiple taoists. It's a great way to figure out how to effectively use many of the tiles and powers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
What can I say about this wonderful game? Co-op games seem to be the flavor of the week for designers and for members of my gaming group as well. I've played quite a few of them that have come out recently... Battlestar Galactica, Pandemic, Arkham Horror, Castle Panic. All of those games are certainly good and have some qualities that make them worth a play, but none of them have what I feel makes Ghost Stories a great game.

The amount of decision making in this game is superb. Some find it random because you are rolling dice to exorcise ghosts. I would think that those are the people that win this game even more rarely than I do. Luck is a small factor in this game compared to skill. The fact that this game can offer so many great decisions in such a short play time is wonderful for me! I can knock a game of this out in less than an hour! Usually all of those involved are willing to play again as well. The sense of satisfaction that you get when you win this game is great. It's certainly hard, it will certainly beat you down, but it's most certainly worth the purchase.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.8
Another co-op game that I have trouble getting into.  You are playing against a preset sequence of moves from the "opponent" and you come up with an optimum way to do your turn (as in all games).  The difference with coops is once you find an optimum way to conduct your turn, you can continue to use this method and the "opponent" will never react, will never change strategies, and the only way you can lose is due to poor dice rolls.

RATING: 8
Played 1 solo play, 3 two way, and one 3 way in a single session back to back. That alone should speak to the quality of the game. Will have to revise my comment after further play, but my initial impression is that it is deliciously playtested to ensure maximum tension, we've come down to a (ineffective) showdown with wei feng each time, once losing because of running out of cards in the deck, once losing by rolling ONE less black die than needed. Hard to imagine beating it on the harder settings atm, but pandemic was the same way at first. Very interested in looking at the expansions for this as well.

Initial impression was that the dice rolling makes for both moments of incredible camaraderie (BLANK ON THE CURSE DIE!) and also reduces quarterbacking, because there is some element of chance in most things you do. Great game.

RATING: 8.5
This is a really fun co-op game but geez is it bloody hard to win.  

You play as Kung-Fu fighters defending a Chinese village from marauding ghosts, many of which are downright ugly.  Beautiful artwork and design, in particular the modular board.

Short, sharp moves with lots of competing decisions throughout.  The only criticism I would make is the iconography is not as intuitive as it could have been.  

Nonetheless this is still a great game and loads of fun even when you are being trounced by all those ghosts.

If you are into co-ops, this is a game worth considering.  Just be prepared to lose a LOT.

EDIT: The more I play this game the more I love it despite the difficulty.  Thematically the game just hangs together beautifully, there's always a level of frantic desperation and the game almost demands player must co-operate to survive.  Ticks lots of boxes for me.  Rating up from 7 to 8.5 and likely to go higher.

RATING: 7.5
{5 plays • 3 & 4 player} Well, I know there are people out there winning at this game, but I'm 0-5 so far... and kind of enjoying it.  What's really nice is that we always feel like we're doing really well during the first half, and then things get hairy, but it still seems like we have a chance.

And then our asses get kicked :)

What's also nice here is that there are enough different options for any one player to do on their turn - many of them equally good (though maybe I'm not one to judge that, having never won) - and because of that, no single player has dominated play, as can often happen with cooperative games.  I'd like to think that no one I'd play with would do this anyway, but it's a plus that the game system also kinda prevents this.

Like most co-op games, I worry that once I win a few times, I'll lose interest.  Especially here, where I've never felt caught up in the theme - like in, say, Pandemic, or even better, Lord of the Rings.

Still, some nice, fresh ideas.  And a pretty nifty challenge.

A good game worth playing that I think one won't play for years and then maybe never touch it again. But if you like cooperative games, this is a must play.

RATING: 8.5
This game has always been kind of an enigma for me.  I don't play it all that often and it kicks my butt when I do.  So, I'm not sure why I like it so much, but I do.  Granted, I'm a fan of asian art stylings, which this has.  I like the simplicity of "guard the village", but love the fact each spot in the village gives you abilities.  I like the fact you can play this solo - which says a lot, I rarely ever play solo games (prefer human interaction).  But, there's just a cool thing happening here as the ghosts descend on the village and you have to priority plan where to take the hits and where not to.  I have only won this game once, but it felt like a million bucks as I took down the final boss.  If you haven't played this, the rules take a bit to sink in (what does this tao do again, can I execute this attack, etc), but it's worth it.  Side note, this definitely has a "Big Trouble In Little China" feel to it, and I was hoping someone would reskin that IP on this game (which now seems unlikely with the Legendary game that came out this past year).  But, one can dream.

RATING: 7.5
A cooperative game for 1 to 4 players.

If you can win this game even on easy level you're probably messing up some rules because this game is almost impossible to win, even on easy and that's what makes it stupid. Instead of making a winnable game on easy level thus motivating players to raise it's dificulty, designers when for a completely frustrating experience making players lose every single time..

The game is hardest with 4 players, with 3, 2 and solo it gets increasingly easier, because you can use other monks abilities on your turn by the use of power tokens.

The taoist powers aren't balanced. But the worst thing is the luck in the dice, even though you're rolling dice you have to prepare for the bad rolls (you have to make sure you have enough tao tokens to exorcise ghosts, but while you're doing that ghosts are pilling up, and soon will be impossible to kill them at a decent pace). In this game a bad roll could cost you the game, because at the rate ghosts appear you can't afford to have a whole turn wasted by a bad dice roll.

It's quite frustating when the dice don't roll in your favor, you end up wasting a turn and not be able to eliminate any ghost (this has been just slightly improved with an artifact of the White Moon expansion). With the haunting ghosts moving forward every round it's irritating to have a whole turn wasted, sure you can sometimes use Tao tokens and maybe have the right Tao token on the Circle of Prayer tile but even that sometimes doesn't help.
You can't rely on the dice, but you have to be constantly rolling them.... Yeah...

When playing solo you can use the roll power of the green taoist, and the yellow taoist power to draw tao token in order to have enough tao tokens to exorcise ghosts. When playing alone the budas are especially useful to use on your own board to exorcise the more dificult black ghosts.

Rules poorly written, but there's a post on this site with the corrected rules.

Lastly, the difficulty level on this kills the fun of the game, next time do some real playtesting.

Played mostly on IOS.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Tipps:

- if the red player board is full, he lose a Qi but he does NOT draw a ghost. When your board is full you do not draw a ghost, you just lose a Qi.

Q : If I draw a ghost and place it on another player board, who is subjected to its effects?
A : The owner of the board is subjected to the effects of a ghost (Qi loss, inactivated power) 

Q : What happens when the Enfeeblement Mantra is placed on a ghost with a resistance of 1?
A : It will automatically be discarded when an exorcism is performed, it works like the 'Circle of Prayer'. It is never discarded immediately

Q : If the 'Circle of Prayer' tile is haunted, what happens if a tao token is present?
A : The tao token is put back to the reserve

RATING: 10
beautiful art.
Fantastic Game.
Easily the best co-op I've EVER played.

Notes for review:
The trick with Ghost Stories is, you don't know what KIND of game you are going to get. In most cases, yes, you use all of the main ghosts (and a random selection of one or more boss ghosts depending on difficulty). The villages are the same, but in different locations each time so you can't optimize which village to hit because you don't know where it will be.

The ghost ordering determines the speed of the game and complexity (outside of the selected challenge level). For example, you could get a series of tough to kill ghosts then a handful of ghosts that trash your resources and you get totally hosed unless you play perfectly. You could get a series of ghosts which spawn new ghosts filling up all the boards. You could get tough haunters which swamp the players on opposite corners of the boards. Or you could get a serious of wimpy ghosts that pop like zits when you stare at them.

Being able to work in different flows is very important to this game and should not be ignored. I've found having several people watching and coaching during the game really helps. The game is VERY difficult to play perfectly, but when everyone plays a strategy right you can pull out a win in even the most dire circumstances.

There is truth that the game has a huge luck factor. I spent a whole game never being able to kill a black ghost. My failure was in not hedging against that by collecting the black tokens. Wise use of resources can mitigate most of the luck in this game.

As far as the limited variable powers, sure, there are only 8 powers with four in play, but the magic isn't in what one player can do...it's about combos. What is the most awesome combo you can pull off with the abilities you are given. And moreover, the order they go on makes a huge difference. Some combos can't be used if the colors are in the wrong order.

The game is a lot deeper than people give it credit for. Many will dismiss it as luck, but the reality is, this is one of the toughest strategy games out there.

I do wish they'd given you an extra dice though...

RATING: 8
Ghost Stories..... What an interesting game. It is probably the game where the gameplay scales the best. It is great as a solitaire as well as with other players. 

Rules and Gameplay are fairly simple but it takes some time to fully understand the Iconography. But you should get it all right after 2-3 plays.

Quality is ok but a far cry from outstanding. I think the best items in the game are the Ghost tokens. The Cards, Board Game tiles and player boards are of mediocre quality.
However, this is not an overly expensive game and the quality is good enough for this kind of game.


The Gameplay is fast paced and absolutely relentless. A round consist of Moving your Token, perform an Action (attack or requesting help) moving Enemy Tokens and drawing a Ghost card.

Now, you will NEVER draw a good card from the Ghost deck. It will always be bad. The card you draw only ranges from bad to very bad.

You also only have 2 rounds to kill a haunting ghost after you drew it or you will loose one of your 9 Village tiles.

It is pure stress. Everything can change at any given time and no one game will be the same.


I found that winning this game is VERY satisfactory. I makes me feel I actually achieved something. In my opinion, this is a great game.

If you enjoy games that will put you constantly under pressure and plays fantastically with all player counts (1-4) than this game should be in your collection.

RATING: 7
Ghost Stories is the first successful design of renowned author Antoine Bauza.

It is a full coop game about defending a chinese village from hordes of ghosts and the incarnations of Wu-Feng (an all powerful necromantic badass) trying to come back from the grave. One to four Taoist monks use their Kung fu to stop Wu-Feng and save the world...
This is more easily said than done, because the game is quite hard, even at the first (out of four) level of difficulty.

The rules are more convoluted and less elegant than those other popular coops (i.e. Pandemic) and the rulebook is not among the best, but after a three or four turns of the first game, everything clicks and gameplay flows smoothly.

The game is a giant, brain-hurting puzzle, and obviously suffers from the "leading/charismatic/experienced player dominating others" syndrome like many other coops. But it is nevertheless quite enjoyable, and also quite thematic.

Rating would probably be even higher if I'd enjoy coops more.

Bauza's talents as a designer are confirmed once more.

RATING: 7
We have games about ancient rural settlements in China, about ancient civilizations in China, about ancient railways in China but we still had no game about ancient monks fighting horrors in China: now we have and any fan of Chinese wuxia or B-movies should rejoice about Ghost Stories, which has a pretty misleading title because, although there’s plenty of ghosts and other nightmarish creatures, there’s no story to be told but the endless and respiteless struggle of your taoist monks working together to keep hordes of monsters at bay.

A somewhat tough task, since there are just too many of them and too few of you: nonetheless, if you manage to look beyond the clumsy and fiddly rules and start caring for the theme (supported by astounding comics-like pieces of art), you could even enjoy it.
Provided you manage to survive.

RATING: 5
I've played many cooperative games, and among those I've played, Ghost Stories is a good game but one of my less-favourite ones.  Pluses and minuses:

+ The cooperation is strong.  A lot more teamwork than in the others I've played, lots of teaming up to accomplish short-term tasks.  Good stuff.

+ Mechanistically, it's one of the best-playing co-ops I've played.  Interesting decisions and room for planning.

- Really only playable with exactly 4 players.  The special rules for handling fewer players are non-intuitive and I don't want to teach the game's special rules to accommodate non-optimum number of players.

- Everything you've heard about high difficulty is true.  I gave everyone five Qi, and threw in some forgiving house rules (like ghosts that draw other ghosts don't cascade past the second) and we still got our asses handed to us such that it felt like we didn't stand a chance.

I want to elaborate on this last point.  Of course everyone wants a challenging co-op, but it should still feel possible.  In this game, one bad choice can throw the game, and you need to be extremely lucky just to have a chance (then still lose from a bad die roll on the final boss).

The most frustrating thing is that in this game, more than any other, you can see two-thirds through the game with stunning clarity that you have already lost... then you have to play another 20 minutes.  When all boards are full, you can lose life, you can un-haunt tiles, to delay losing the game outright... but with no new ghosts coming in, you're no closer to [u]winning[/u] the game either, so all you're doing is delaying the inevitable.  Wheeee!

It's ridiculously hard such that you need extreme luck to give yourself the chance that more extreme luck will get you to the bad guy so you have the extreme lucky chance of finishing him.  The mechanisms are a way to use your brain to keep from losing, but you can only win with laughably long lucky streaks.

Some people say you need to play the game a dozen times before you have a chance...  Okay, sure, but how can I introduce this game to new players and tell them, we're definitely going to lose our first several games?  Who would want to even bother learning?  Let's take it for granted we've lost and play something else instead.

RATING: 7
Having played most of the prominent cooperative games, Ghost Stories was one of the more entertaining ones.  However, it suffers the common flaw of lack of narrative.  The entire game is you killing ghosts and the fundamentals of that activity don't really change.  And the tension doesn't really ramp up, it's not like the number of ghosts or their difficulty slowly creeps up as the game progresses.

My other problem are the player powers.  The options within and among the colors often diverge wildly in power and certain ones (like the double action blue power) encourage really boring strategies like sitting on the Buddha.

That said, Ghost Stories takes a spot right behind LotR and Pandemic in my estimation of cooperative games.

RATING: 8
Great coop-Game here, with beautiful art work. After one game I can say it tops the strong pandemic.
At all it seems tougher to win as in pandemic. 
The turns of the players are short and can be summarized as: 
Draw a ghost card, place it on one players board, use a village action or banish a ghost card and at last, if you have a buddha figure, place it optinonally on a empty ghost card space in front of you Monk (if a card is placed on a space with a buddha the card will be effectless discarded, which is great). 

There are a lot of small decions, e.g  where to place the ghost cards, which village actions should be used etc. But most important is the permanent time-pressure, will you go to banish the most threatening ghost but the tougher one, or a weaker but easier to defeat one. Or is it better to invest an action to use the help of the village people e.g. take one or mores precious Tao-Tiles. In the end also good dice rolls are needed to win, but that’s fine for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I really like this game, but I can only give it a 7 because it is so relentlessly difficult that it's almost required you modify a few of the rules before it's any fun.
I enjoy soul crushingly difficult cooperative gaming experiences, like Shadows Over Camelot and Eldritch Horror, but Ghost Stories is almost over-the-top in its level of challenge.
To make the game a little more manageable, me and my wife delay the haunters so they're haunting once every three turns instead of once every two turns, we strategically place the villages rather than doing so randomly, and we try to roll the curse die on an axis so that it's more likely to land on one of the empty squares. Without those three very simple modifications, this game's difficulty is so relentless it's not even fun. 
I really like Ghost Stories, and it's really great for those who love getting brutally raped by a game that loathes its players' existence for having the audacity to open its packaging, but the challenge is overwhelming at the easiest difficulty settings if you don't slightly modify the rules.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Fun game...Complicated enough to win to make it a nice challenge.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Individual powers and pawns are key to making each player feel like they are personally playing a game and not some kind of group solitaire, although the red powers are disappointingly dull compared to the other three colours.

The scaling difficulty is great because the game is really really difficult when you first learn how to play. Even now I still don't play on Hell level.

I love that you can gamble and hope to roll well to exorcise a ghost, but that really the dice should be used to minimise how much you'll be paying. It's completely counter-intuitive, but it's required in order to do well at the game.

Between the changing of the layout of the village, the different powers available per colour, the different Wu-Fengs, and the variety of ghosts (not all of which you'll face in every game), the game feels fresh every time.

Due to the rapid rate at which ghosts are spawned, plans rarely go further than two turns into the future.

The rules for how to play with less than four are great. They flow well and they don't feel tacked on.

I love that the box cover features a man and a woman, although I would have liked to see that reflected in the pawns as well (the pawns are all male). 

I like how there are women on the town tiles, although I would have liked to have seen more of them.

I shouldn't have to say the following, but will due to the sorry state of affairs in board games:

I like that there are no white people in this game because they would be out of place. But I've come to expect white people in all games because apparently companies believe that white people won't buy games without white people in them, but non-white people will buy games without non-white people in them.

I love that the people are not caricatures, which is so often the case for European/American games.

I love that they didn't use the Ching Chong font, a staple of Europeans and Americans who want to show Asianess (like when those say Europeans and Americans pull on the corners of their eyes and says ching chang chong to show Asianess).

Yes, I long for the day when I don't praise a game for being not racist.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
FF Green
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Most good co-op games have a fun puzzley feeling to them, and I find Ghost Stories particiularly enthralling in this regard. The village tiles are a pretty simple way to obscure optimal plays, making it feel especially puzzley and replayable. There's usually a number of ways to deal with any given situation - mostly to do with which tiles you're going to make use of in which order - and so usually when you lose it feels like you should have made other choices, which, I think, is key to replayability.

Now, it's true there are dice and there is a lot of luck in this game. More than Pandemic? Probably, or at least it feels more unforgiving, but honestly the dice are the least of your worries here. Optimal plays generally involve either increasing your odds of success before even attempting a roll, or bypassing rolling entirely, so losing due to poor rolls is actually somewhat rare amongst seasoned players (though obviously, it can happen, but usually a lost roll just increases the tension and stakes rather than ends the game).

What feels more random are the ways monsters can combo together in sudden and unexpected ways. I'm sure if you play enough of this you learn what to account for when assessing threats, but because of the ways ghosts can combo just figuring out where your high risk areas even are is much harder here than in Pandemic, which has a lot more known information.

Do you need this if you have other co-op games? I'm gonna go with ...maybe? Probably? In my opinion, this is one of the better ones, so if for whatever reason you want a new co-op adventure, I highly recommend it. There's lots of fun options, loads of tension, a good difficulty level, and the theme and art (well, on the tiles - the cards are more hit-or-miss) are pretty groovy. Pandemic would probably still be my go-to as an intro to the genre, though, because of the excellent expansion options to extend longevity and overall simplicity of rules. I have about equal fun with base game Pandemic and Ghost Stories, but there's lots of little rules to remember, especially during setup, in Ghost Stories that it's harder to just pull out when you've not played in awhile.

Be warned, however, that the rulebook for this game is terrible. I have the first version so maybe it's been cleaned up by now... but not only are things vaguely worded, but poorly organized (especially if you're playing with 2-3 players instead of 4). The rules themselves feel a little daunting at first just given that there's so many little tokens and rules, etc., but thankfully quickly become second nature. AND this is one of the very few games I will praise for its iconography - there's few enough symbols and they're generally clear enough that they're actually understandable even during your first game and speed things up thereafter, rather than just add unnecessary confusion. A+ on those, really and truly.

[u]February 2010:[/u] Just bought

[u]March 2010:[/u] I like it a lot better than Pandemic, it is a LOT harder, we won on initiation mode for the first time at ur 5th play! And that's because luck was on our side! The game is very very challenging, and I expect it to be for quite a long time too. The artwork is gorgeous too and really adds a lot. Right now, I'm having tons of fun with this game.

RATING: 8.5
This is by far the best co-op I’ve ever played! Sure, I haven't played every co-op, but I have played all the popular games like Pandemic, Forbidden Island, Defenders of the Realm, Yggdrasil etc, but this game really is the clear #1 imo! 

It’s so intense and just a pleasure to play! I’m not a big fan of theme and game components, it doesn’t really matter that much to me, but this game has a cool theme and WONDERFUL components and artwork! 

You can only do ONE thing on your turn, but you want to do SO much stuff, so it’s quite frustrating – in a good way! There is much to think about each turn (though it's not prone to AP at all) because you want to do a lot but aren't able to do it as the monsters quickly swarm you! It might start out to be easy, but later in the game it turns out to be really hard. Lots of different monster abilities, different player abilities, different village tile abilities etc. Finally, the gorgeous artwork helps to attract new players and also keeps the experienced players around.

Also, I haven’t seen the “experienced-player-tells-everybody-else-what-to-do” syndrome which can occur in Pandemic and other games. Maybe it’s just me, but it might be because in Pandemic there are usually one or two optimal moves, whereas in Ghost Stories there might be better moves than others, but it’s not like there is THE right move. So everybody can discuss what to do.

I’ve played my fair share of pure co-ops and semi co-ops with many different groups, and this is by far the favorite for me and everybody I’ve played with. Finally, this game has two GREAT expansions which really make the game feel totally different depending on which expansion you use. It means that GS can be played in 4 totally different ways if you want, but I actually prefer the base game on its own.

I want my co-ops to be hard to beat and I want to gasp for breath, and Ghost Stories really gives me that feeling! The difficulty of this game (and the ability to make the game really hard by playing on hell difficulty...) along with two great expansions make this game a winner for me!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Brutal, clever, free flowing and engaging, this "impending doom" coop still stands taller above all other similar games. For me, it blows Pandemic out of the water, due to its stronger puzzle nature. Pandemic, with its brilliant "shuffle back and put on the deck" mechanism, is a highway stroll on a good visibility day gone wrong, whereas Ghost Stories is a cross-country ride in twilight gone terrible from the get go. What stands out in this one is the way the 9-tile grid placement defines the likely strategy, and the general setup variability that the game offers, coupled with the last stand boss battle. This is a masterfully crafted game, and one that I will be certainly playing for years to come.

+ Strong escalation arc that constantly increases the tension towards the final battle
+ Brilliant forward looking and planning cycle
+ The release valves of the yin-yang and Qi provide both an assurance but also a source of desperation
+ Simple, elegant ruleset that can be taught in 10 minutes
+ Short in duration, packing a true cooperative beefy game
+ The theme is bang on, and comes through very well
+ Works equally well solo (with 4 Taoists) to 4 players

= Alpha gamer syndrome is present and needs to be avoided
= Very hard and unforgiving to start with, the way a true coop should be

- Although the art is evoking enough, a darker and more theme-appropriate type of art would make the game even more enjoyable

RATING: 6
Dec. 7, 2008 -- I'd like to play this a few more times before really making a decision about it, but after my first two plays, I'm lukewarm on it. I like the theme. I like the production values. I like some of the mechanics. I even like the cooperative aspect, although I wish there were more ways to cooperate with the other players.

As the ghosts haunt areas of the board, the game becomes tense and hard decisions have to be made. The end-game for a losing situation comes on quickly and everyone has to rush to try to turn the tide. The end-game for a win is anticlimactic, though. The bosses are little more than tough ghosts with a special power or two, and when they're vanquished, it seemed to me it was an "oh, did we just win?" moment.  I expected something a bit more big and intense with the boss battles.

Tentative rating of 6/10.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Got a signed copy which includes a drawing inside the box by the artist. The artwork is absolutely amazing.  

The rules are not always very clear on some points. It does need to be played in order to apply all the rules perfectly. Moreover you need to get a hang of what all the villagers and taoist can do, and when to make use of it.

It is a very nice coop game, that also plays well with two players. You can also play it solo, but then all the decisions are up to you, and you don't have a second opinion on things. 

I do think the game has great replayability and variety, because of the different gamelevels, different incarnations you have to beat in order to win the game, different taoist powers and the setup of the villagetiles. 

Played it with 2 players mostly and a couple of times with 3. We won 1 time, and lost all the others. It is hard, but exciting and I can see improvement, but we still need to find a perfect strategie to beat the game.

Getting a bit frustrated with the game, Because my sis and I cant seem to win. We won't give up though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Ghost Stories is a story of the downfall of good intentions and great expectations. My interest in this title when it was announced before Spiel 2008 was immediate: strong subject matter, colourful and evocative artwork, and cooperation. Repos may as well have offered crack-on-a-stick for all I cared. I bought the game after a quick session in which about 10 ghosts were dispatched and then took the game with me on holiday to play a few solo games. Welll... they didn't go as I had hoped. I was quickly overrun from all sides and after two frustrating evenings put the game away. Then I started playing with other people and watched my initial enthusiasm burn away, to replaced with disbelief, which then gave away to plain exasperation, eventually ending up in indifference. We could not win a single game in the +/- 15 I played, we rarely succeeded in getting Wu-feng on the boards, even. The feeling of fighting a losing battle soon became too overpowering for me to enjoy the game much, and as a result the game has been gathering dust ever since.

I have thought long and hard about this, especially since there are people who are obviously full of enthusiasm for this game. Once the initial confusion about the rules subsided, it turned out that many wins against the game were achieved in 'solo mode' where some rules have been introduced to make up for the fact that no live players participate. The game is easier to play under these circumstances as the power tokens allow for powerful combos to appear which do not exist in the genuine multiplayer game; also, the ghost deck is smaller. A few experienced soloplayers have offered to try to beat the game at the lowest level in 'multiplayer mode' with some tweaks to make the game as hard as possible; and to their credit (and, admittedly, my amazement) they succeeded, but not without a big amount of trouble, and certainly not as smoothly as in solo mode. I've been forced to revise my opinion that the game is therefore 'doable' on all low levels, although I don't really see people winning multiplayer games on the most difficult levels Nightmare and Hell in all but exceptional cases.

The question then becomes one of it being [i]fun[/i] to play. Opinions on that of course differ. I think that for a coop to succeed, players should have a certainty that their planned actions succeed with at least a very high probability. Ghost Stories fails on that account: just look at the tao dice. You can [i]take[/i] an exorcism-action, but in a lot of cases you don't know whether it will succeed or not. Such a pronounced element of chance ruins the game for me. (Once I realised this, I could also explain why a coop like Witches of Salem provokes the same level of distate.) I don't like the idea of playing a game and then realising the outcome was not only due to me playing a sound strategy or applying sound tactics, but also because the dice and cards cooperated or may have cooperated. (After all, in solo mode impressive win rates have been mentioned, so [i]there[/i] it cannot be all chance.) I find it very hard to disentangle good play from chancy play in this game, especially while in multiplayer mode, and as a result I haven't touched it in quite a while. I prefer Pandemic and even the ageing Lord of the Rings coops, simply because there [i]everything[/i] a player does has precise consequences. It is understandable why a designer would want to introduce an element of randomness into these certainties, but the price—loss of control—is not one I am willing to pay for a coop.

There is another issue at work with Ghost Stories, but it took me a long while to realise it. Ghost Stories is not really a game about [i]winning[/i], it's a game about [i]not losing[/i]. The monks—the players—are continously losing life force, tao, yin-yang, and sometimes even their special abilities. The question is whether they can sustain those losses until some arbitrary cut-off point, which in this game means the final incarnation of Wu-feng. Now contrast to a coop which does things right (say, Pandemic): the players themselves never lose anything. Instead there are just anonymous timers of a kind to force the players to hurry up. This is too a kind of not losing, but on a much more subdued and abstracted level.

[b]Update[/b] The game never got played anymore, and I so let it go to a home where it would be looked after better.

RATING: 8.5
If you like challenging co-op games this is for you, the mechanics and theme are top notch. If your group doesn't like stiff challenges then steer away.

 Indeed, 2 player games are super hard to win, but if you do eventually manage to win then it feels like you had just conquered the world. Three and four player games are a bit easier but still, this game comes at you and never-ever lets up trying to beat you down, making victory all that much sweeter.

My only complaint about this game is the rule book, it is a little clunky and badly laid out but once you learn the system the game is a true gem.

RATING: 8
[2012-04-30 Rating: n.a. -> 8]
I ignored Ghost Stories for a long time. Something about this game just didn't click with me. It was the release of the iOS version that pushed me over the edge and made me try the game. After a handful of solo games on the IPad, I was sold. The game is brutally hard and I haven't won any of my games yet. But each play is such a nice puzzle. It's so much fun to figure out the best way to deal with all the bad stuff which the game throws at you. Ghost Stories is a real nice solo game and the usage of the iOS spares you the burden of the setup.

One thing I haven't made up my mind about is whether I like Ghost Stories if it's played as a real coop game and not in solo mode. In my non-solo games a lot of the puzzle like experience I value so much was replaced with long discussions about which move to make. Not that there is something wrong about debating with your friends, but somehow I value the strict puzzle solving nature of the solo game more than the social aspect of the coop experience. 

So as it stands now, my rating of 8 is for the solo mode. Played with more players this rating drops to a 7 for me. Maybe this will change after a couple more games.

RATING: 8
One of the most beautifully illustrated board games anywhere and a coop game with no equal.  People who don't like coops won't be converted but there is much to love here.

The theme in this game is wonderful and creative.  It's such a staple of Hong Kong cinema that getting a game about kung fu monks battling the undead of Chinese folklore is a stroke of genius.

This is basically a game of judging odds and making educated guess about the best path through the perils.  In a sense, this is all you do and it could seem repetitive.  I like dice odds and so this works well for me and there are enough special factors to keep it interesting throughout.

This is also a highly difficult game.  So much so that anyone who finds it to be easy almost certainly has made rules mistakes.  There is a perverse compulsion to keep playing until victory.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Russell
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Players are fighting back ghosts from taking over a village.  Beautiful looking cooperative game, where players take turns to introduce a ghost, and then take a turn doing something in the village.  Players can move, then either try to banish a ghost, or use the ability on that village space.  Ghosts gradually encroach on the village and eventually begin haunting village tiles, negating the village space ability.  Players win if you can survive until the "boss" ghost appears, and dispatch it.  Nicely produced game with a fantastic Eastern/anime look, solid rules and game play, and just the right sense of growing dread as you are snowed under with ghosts.  Felt very similar in style to Shadows over Camelot and Pandemic, where you advance evil and then do something about it.  Much better game play than Shadows, but because everything is open the cooperative table bully can run the game for everyone.  I'm finding it best as a solo game, or a two player with my wife.  Space Alert is the latest king of cooperative games; Ghost Stories, while beautiful, blends in with the rest.

RATING: 7.5
I have played several solo games where I controlled 1/2/3/4 monks.  This game is growing on me.  I find the rules easy to explain.  At first, the game seems heavy where symbols are concerned, but once you have the symbology, it flows rather quickly.
Recently, I played a 3-player game.  We lost, and had a discussion.  We find that even though you are able to use the 'Neutral' monk's power (if you have power tokens), lacking the neutral monk's action phase (Yang phase), while observing the Yin phase (ie. the Ghost phase) slants the game in Wu-Feng's favour.  A such, we feel it is a 1, 2, or 4 player game - ie. All monks need to be active if you plan to have a hope in Wu-Feng to win.
This game is on it's way to becoming my favourite co-op game.

Update: Finally played a 4 player game vs. [thing=54883][/thing] & won (on the easy level) by the skin of our teeth.

4 players is where this gem shines.

RATING: 10
Best co-op in the business. That's right i said best, you better believe it, yes better than pandemic.....yes way better than spirit island. Why? the puzzle my friend that's why!

you see some of you guys will see this game as an extremely difficult non stop influx of ghosts that just can't be dealt with never mind the boss if you even get to see him that is!!!

but seriously that's not what this game is about. You see the puzzle is a puzzle of survival and tactics to make the most out of the 9 villages there to help you. Most people i have played with after failing the first run of the game miserably want to try again employing new better thought out tactics. They can visibly see how much closer thay get to the boss!

The best games are ones that leave you dissecting every move making you think what you could have done better. When that win comes the feeling of self satisfaction is like conquering a great challenge and there arn't that many games in the business that can do that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is the game that got me interested in co-ops again!  Arkham Horror is also a horror-ish co-op, but Ghost Stories scratches a similar itch, plays so much quicker, and doesn't have nearly as many fiddly bits.  The art is so well done in this game that I feel it alone was worth the price of admission.  It's great that this game can be played solo and the special abilities of the villagers/taoists make the game fun.  I really like that the rulebook provides many ways to tweak the difficulty and provides the ability to score your performance.  It's great that there's no semi-hidden information either, which is a pet peeve of mine when it comes to other co-ops.  The only negative thing I can say about it, is that the rulebook doesn't clarify so many of the situations that can occur in the game.  At least there's BGG with a FAQ.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[b]Rating based on - 7 plays, 2 player[/b]
I recently got this as a birthday present from my other half. So far we are having fun, but maybe that is because it's still in the honeymoon phase. I think the only way to enjoy this game is to start out knowing that you will never win. It is brutally difficult, and you can discuss about strategy all you want but this is a luck based game. It has both dice AND cards. In my opinion, the power tokens are rubbish for 2 players. Every turn you have either a ghost to battle or new ghost coming out. You have no time to keep running back to the centre tile to pick up tokens when you are being overrun. The only way to play properly with 2 is to control 2 monks each and use the powers of the monks 'real time'. The rule book is abominable. I don't understand why foreign language publishers are too cheap to invest in a native English speaker to proofread their rules and cards for spelling and grammatical errors. Geez! I'd do it for free just to avoid the aggravation!
[b]Status: KEEPER[/b]

Mel: Cool theme, one of the few co-ops that really encourages COOPERATION instead of a leader barking orders at soldier monkeys a la Space Alert. I like to use it as a gateway game because the theme is "cute" enough to get non or new gamers to consider playing, but requires a lot of strategic thinking (which doesn't really occur to said players until after it's over).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This game has always been quite popular with the BGG crowd, but frankly, I don't get it. Is it the oriental theme that I have little affinity for or is it the game play? As to the game play, it's a surprisingly simple game once you learn how to play and understand the iconography. I mean, very simple. Run around and collect chits and try to roll colors you want. That's pretty much it. There's not much of an arc to the game. What I was doing on turn 25 was the exact same thing I was doing on turn 1.  Every turn is the same.  I think it'd do well to have a day and night phase or two halves of the game or something to indicate a passage of time and have things change instead of just doing the same thing over and over. 

Furthermore, it's the least cooperative game of the three old school coops. You don't really cooperate so much as just play all on the same side. Not a bad game, but nothing special IMO either. 

For my money, I much prefer Knizia's LOTR coop over the other two old school coops, Pandemic and Ghost Stories, and after having played LOTR not till after both of those, I'm not sure I get why people went gaga for those two when the LOTR design offers more interesting choices and variation. The hand of cards you have offers more individual decisions than either of those. From my experience, I would've guessed the order was Ghost Stories > Pandemic > LOTR.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
I love, love, love:
- the artwork
- the colorful board
- playing co-op
- the replayability
- asymmetric player powers

I dislike:
- always forgetting what the Tao tokens and Yin-Yang tokens do
- the rulebook's poor organization and occasional typos
- player elimination
- ever getting to choose where to place a ghost

Final verdict: Enjoyable game that's difficult to win, fun to play, and a good way to spend time, but being able to choose where to place a ghost is weird, as it takes away from the theme but does allow you to strategize.

RATING: 8
Pros
-Different theme than zombies
-Hard to win, but still satisfying on lost
-Cooperative and moderate game length
-4 very unique characters (with alternate abilities on each)

Cons
-Some locations don't seem as useful

RATING: 7
I think it's fair to compare it to Pandemic because the gameplay  has a Pandemic feel but with lots more chrome and things going on.  I have to say the card deck of ghosts is much more interesting than a stack of locations like in Pandemic.  I think the variety of ghosts and their illustrations is the best part of the game and give it a lot of personality.  The artwork is great (looks better in person than in photos on the Geek) and the icons look tough at first but are not so bad in reality.  I think it's a winner.  To me it feels like a bigger, longer more immersive Pandemic with a creepy theme.  One gripe:  the cheesy plastic monks look out of place next to the cool Buddha bits and otherwise great components.

Update:  I geeked out and painted my monks.  Now the game looks perfect.

RATING: 6
A very hard coop with interesting twists. The jury is still out on this one. It could easily drop to a 5 or raise to a 7. It essentially depends whether the difficulty comes from randomness or from the hard decision-making. I'm suspecting you have to get lucky to beat this one, in which case it would start to look like a boring "solitaire": draw the right card, roll the right dice and win! However, if it appears that you can beat it through good planning and strong play it could shine as one of the toughest and renewable coop game. 

Also note that this one exacerbates the "strongest-player-decides-everything" problem of many coop games since all the information is visible. The only game that I know of that really solves this problem is Space Alert.

RATING: 6
Ghost Stories isn't all that different from most other cooperative games. There is a threat (evil spirits in this case) that increases as the game moves along. If the players get their priorities right and aren't too unlucky in their card draws and dice rolls they will likely beat the challenge.

The theme carries over pretty well in this one, but it is lacking a game arc apart from what the randomly drawn cards provide. Actions available to the players stay pretty much the same throughout. Admittedly, that is another trait that it shares with many other coops.

The dark artwork and constant creep of the surrounding haunter figurines make this game incredibly claustrophobic and thematic. I had nightmares after the first night I played it!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b]INITIAL COMPLAINTS[/b] - Strictly a solitaire game.  With other cooperative games, there is at least a modicum of concealment with players having hands of cards that cannot be displayed.  Even if you're allowed to tell your teammates what cards you have, there is still the need to communicate and the need to involve everyone in the planning.  In Ghost Stories, a player can just stare at the board and the chips in front of each player and come up with the "right" move.  Someone else might have a better idea, or they might not, but in any case they're doing exactly the same analysis you're doing.

[b]UPDATE[/b] - My opinion of Ghost Stories has improved markedly after resigning myself to the fact that it's a solitaire game. Playing solitaire (with four Taoists) is an enjoyable puzzle on Nightmare or Hell levels. For solitaire play, I would rate Ghost Stories a 9 (with the Guardhouse expansion). As a multi-player cooperative game, I would rate it a 6 - I would much rather play Lord of the Rings or Space Alert or Hanabi or Pandemic.

RATING: 5
As far as game mechanics go, this one was interesting and compelling as a co-op.

I do not really like the theme, but especially do not like the bizarre cultural syncretism between taoism, buddhism, the undead, and horror. The artwork, though facially intended to be slightly humorous, is macabre and uninvitingly dark.

If the game had a different theme, I would certainly own it and play it again. But the theme is a big turn off. I won't rate the game because I would honestly have to put it below a 5 for theme and artwork alone. For game mechanics, though, it's well above a 7, possibly above an 8.

The BGG ratings have no accounting for subjective taste in anything other than the game as a whole, and my thoughts about it are too disjointed for me to be fair about it.
(2014-07-08)

I've decided to rate it anyway.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Not a bad cooperative game, and I liked it at first, but it's repetitive and can become a little boring. On most turns, you draw and place a ghost, resolve their powers, then move your character (or not) and either activate a tile or roll dice to exorcise a ghost. Choices are very limited, with most tile powers being circunstancial and rarely (if ever) used. The theme is the main appeal of the game, but it's just not there, even with the nice miniatures. As for the artwork, I like the use of color, but I'm not a fan of the cartoony style. Also, the difficulty to win can vary a lot depending on various random factors and even the number of players. It's probably best played solo with all characters.

RATING: 8
kici kung-fu szerzetes szétrúgni szellem se..ed
Ismét egy távol-keleti téma a tervezőtől, ráadásul elég brutális erősségben. Ez a kihívás faktor valakinek vagy kerülendő, vagy épp ez teszi vonzóvá.
Első találkozásra simán a túlvilágról visszatérő szellemek nyertek, alig éreztem azt, hogy kici kínai szerzeteseink irányítanának bármit is, csak sodrottunk a támadók áradatával.
Pár játék és a szabályok rendes áttanulmányozása után azért már növekszik az esély, hatásos fegyverré válik a kung-fu. Mivel minden körben új kíséretek jelennek meg, a falu védelme sosem könnyű, folyamatosan mérlegelni kell, mit is tegyenek a négyek a lehető legjobban kiaknázva a képességeikben rejlő potenciált. Néha ez elég, néha nem.
Ráadásul a játék utolsó köreiben (ha a szerencsések eljutnak odáig egyáltalán), megjelenik az ördögi vufeng és ő grabancát kell elkapni a győzelemhez.
Szép a játék kivitele is, igaz kicsit csalódás a kockák minősége (kopnak, de rendesen). A szabályokat, a négyek és a falulapkák különleges képességeit azért érdemes rendesen megismerni, bár könnyen tanulhatóak. Mindenképpen kell pár (vagy több) játék, hogy megismerd a benne rejlő lehetőségeket. Aki ezt rááldozza, sok élménnyel lehet gazdagabb.
Nekem egyik kedvencem, szívesen ajánlom azoknak, aki keresik a kihívásokat és el tudják fogadni, hogy itt dolgozik bizony a szerencse is és bármilyen jól alakultak is addig a dolgaink, akár egyetlen új szellem elég és rögtön a földi pokolban érezzük magunkat.

RATING: 8
Great game, a must have for everyone, as it makes a perfect game for Halloween.

I love: The design. It is superb to look at, great art and it has miniature.

I don't mind: The randomness of the card draw. Drawing a bad set of ghosts (especially those who force you to draw again) can bring the game to a swift conclusion, but after several plays, you should know this will happen.

I hate: Re-playability of the basic game. I wish there were more village tiles available, so that there were less obvious series of actions in certain situations: such as "go here first, and take this action, next player does this and take this action, which means that we are a in perfect position to take down this big ghost". Feels very systematic. Finally, GS suffers from a very bad case of leader player, where 1 player dictates every one's action.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A very neat game with awesome art and superb solo playability. The rules for solo play are very reasonable and balanced, and while it is also possible to play with four monks (like with four players), playing with one monk plus the rules is just as haunting an experience.

The game is pretty random. Even with a good strategy, and after a few lucky rolls, it's still possible to draw a combination of ghosts that totally screws you. And the die rolls when ghosts haunt tiles, while always dangerous, can end the game quickly if you're unlucky.

All this however makes the game all the more challenging, in a good way, and personally I never felt like I was only at the mercy of the dice. There's always plays available that can minimize the dependance on luck, and you better find those, because you can count on eventually getting unlucky otherwise.

RATING: 3
First play, lost & loved it.. it is very hard, something i like. I have to play some more though, my concern (as with any Co-op games) is, that once you have figured out the best strategy, it won't make any sense to deviate from it.. at wich point the game plays itself basically. But then there is the Black Secrets expansion wich could remedy that by making it 1 vs. many.. let's see.

Down from 8 to 4.. figured out the best strategy.. now it's boring. Common Problem with most co-ops.

Down from 4 to 3.. the mechanics are not so easily figured out, so people who are not good in deducting the best strategy make everyone else loose.. on the other hand if the clever ones tell them always what to do.. they would become superfluous.. man how i hate playing straight co-ops..

!Spoilers!

Best Strategy (imho) is:
Blue: double actions, gets 2 buddhas every 2'nd round, every other turn fights two times on corner & places both buddhas.
Yellow: token generation, gets more tokens and stays with green preferably on a corner.
Green: reroll, stays with yellow preferably at corner and kills 2 ghosts a turn with the help of yellows tokens.
Red: 1 other player move, helps out, places the weakening colored token & kills with Qi the tough ones.

RATING: N/A
roffster
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
7 Wonders is often seen as Antoine Bauza's crown jewel, but for me it has to be Ghost Stories. Ghost Stories is just about everything I want in a game. It's challenging with lots of options. It has a great theme. The complexity to payoff ratio is off the charts. It rewards multiple plays and subtle strategy.

It's unfortunately seen as too random by some, and I can understand that. Ghost Stories was on my trade list for a bit after my first few plays, but sticking with it really paid off. Ghost Stories is a game about risk and action optimization. The deck is symmetrical giving you insight into what can and cannot happen later in the game. The dice are a risk but smart play can allow you to flip a situation from a risk of whiffing an action to a random chance of saving resources for later. The game is unforgiving to mistakes particularly with how you position your samurai and gives you many subtle cues as to how you should be playing each turn.

My absolute favorite part of the game is the pacing. Games all tend to start slowly allowing you to start setting up your initial strategy. The deck can play out a few different ways from a constant threat to an explosive start followed by a lull, and recognizing how the game is playing out is a key to playing well. So the game has great tactical choices as well as some solid chewiness at a strategic one.

Lastly, the game just plays great solo. The lack of hand management makes it easy to manage multiple samurai, and they are always working together so it feels more like activating a team one-by-one than playing as separate characters. One of my favorite solo games and just one of my favorite games in general 

Best with 1-2 and good with 1-4

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[b]Repos multilingual edition 2008[/b]

- high-quality cardstock (thicker, but slightly smaller, than later editions/expansions)

- godawful rulebook

Rough trade in the form of cardboard and plastic.  A crazy, ever-shifting puzzle that actually prevents immersion in the rich theme.  If you let the mechanical aspects of the game fuzz into the background in order to provide a foundation for the experience of being a Taoist monk desperately fighting the legions of Hell, you will lose.

The game begs you to do so, with gorgeous art and super production values, but ultimately you have to look past the theme and see the grinding gears of the puzzle box if you have any hope of ever winning.  Also, there's an enormous luck component (repeat die rolls to exorcise the ghosts), meaning that even optimal play can be fatally hosed with gallons of demon-tentacle spew.  And the rulebook is... nigh impenetrable.  I'm still not completely sure how some parts of the game work.

For all that, it's an 8?  Yeah—it's stuck with me, I've been thinking about it, and I want to play it again until I beat it to death.

UPDATE:  Dropped to a 7.  Suffers from the same problem most co-op games do, but to a degree I just can't get over:  one person masterminding everyone else's turn.  Perhaps it's better suited to solo play instead of "one guy solves the puzzle while directing three chit-pushers".

[b]Note:[/b]  [i]Later expansion cards don't match this edition.[/i]  They use thinner, slightly larger cards which mangulate when shuffled and are obvious in the deck.  This would be solved by sleeves, if I believed in sleeves, but I don't as they are hateful abominations—an affront to the delicate tactile sensibilities of the human hand.

"But Chris," you say, "in [i]Ghost Stories[/i] you don't hold the cards in your hand!"  But I [i]do[/i] hold them in my hand—as I slap someone smaller and weaker than me, right in front of you, someone who didn't deserve it and would never have gotten slapped in the first place if you hadn't opened your stupid mouth.

(Gave this to the kids.)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[b]Repos English edition 2015[/b]

- thinner, slightly larger cards than earlier editions; matches 2015 printings of expansions

- improved iconography

- vastly improved rulebook

[i]Seven years later.[/i]  Resurrecting this (heh) now that the kids are of age, and whaddya know, the game's pretty good with truly respectful co-op players.  The [i]X-Men[/i]-like teamwork from those who value the sanctity of the individual turn (i.e., we all have something to offer, but your turn is yours, and yours alone) makes the game shine, and allowed us to win for the first time in 6 plays.  And I can see how we might need to actually increase the difficulty... and my rating.

Also:  my mechanic/thematic grumblings above?  Utterly nullified with good players.  With the right people the game feels like it looks, spooky-beautiful.

RATING: 8.5
I guess I am just of a fan of Bauza's designs, cause Ghost Stories is another game I really like. A very hard to win coop game that has you playing as Taoists protecting a village from ghosts. 

The game is one of the simpler games to teach, and like 7 Wonders is language independent with many symbols that pretty much explain what all cards, village tiles and dice do. Yes, the die rolling can be "swingy" but there many ways to help with mitigating dice, such as Tao tokens that help defeat ghosts, different village tiles lowering their resistance, and even the powers of the Taoist themselves. 

A really solid game, which even without expansions, is great. Needs to hit the table more.

RATING: 6
Second game much harder.  I think it has something to do with playing with the correct rules.

A cooperative game in which the players all have different powers they use to defeat the automatically generated threats.  The obvious comparison is to Pandemic, only the results depend on tokens and dice rolls instead of cards.  It's really a game about prioritizing and using available resources. Timing is very important because some ghosts affect how others can be fought.  

Though I liked the claustrophobic feeling of this, with the ghosts closing in around you, I think I prefer Pandemic for this sort of thing because it's a cleaner, less convoluted design.  But then again, this isn't my favorite sort of thing, either. (2 play)

RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Well the first thing you notice is the art, it really grabs your attention and invokes the theme very well. The game scales from 1 to 4 players and from what I can see it would do it well (fairly open system). You can also scale the difficulty easily as well which is another important factor. Gametime will come in around 60 minutes, or potentially less if you get hosed like we did... 

Tension builds quickly here and does not let off once it ramps up. Ghosts start invading and it is pretty challenging trying to keep them under control, we played the easy level and started off good but quicky got smoked around the midgame with no point of return. 

Decision-wise a little more to consider than Pandemic but I'm still not sure how much more really, some of the optimal moves seem obvious but notice I said SOME, I think there were several times where we really had a hard time decided our next best move as once again there are several ways to 'skin the cat' and you just never know which peril might be next. This is where it does surpass Pandemic for me, decisions on where to place ghosts, what actions to take, and every situation looks a little different, you can't just go building 2 or 3 stations spread over the board to help your chances like in Pandemic. 

Replay worried me a little but I think mostly it will be good, I was surprised to see that the 9 tiles for actions that make up the board were the only ones included, I smell an expansion. I do think because of the challenge there will be lots of game in this package, its just that with another even 2 tiles it could have been that much more. Also I think (not sure on this one) that only the 4 roles for the players were included, another role or two could have really added here. Turns do feel somewhat 'samey', this is where something like LOTR bodes well. Don't forget here though, because the main engine is card driven (ghosts invading) the randomness of the ghosts invading should keep each game a little different, also even where you 'place' the ghosts could potentially change the outcome of a game due to what action is directly in front of it. 

Summary - Co-op fans rejoice! Lots to choose from, all we need now is more shelf space to house all these new great games and smaller boxes when possible... (publishers have mercy please!)

RATING: 5
This was a tough, frustrating game. I think a big part of the frustration comes from the dice. It seemed like if a few more rolls went our way we would have been in decent shape, but for a game that's as hard as this to come down to a roll of the dice is just a bit frustrating. And I'm not saying 'oh if only I'd rolled 3 blacks on 3 dice and then the next guy rolled 3 yellows on his 3 dice we'd have won' I'm saying that we failed to kill 1 hp guys with 4 dice a few times. Those are over 80% likely to succeed. And because of the nature of the game we almost never take a shot on less likely fights, so the luck can't really go the other way to even out. When a less random game is hard and you lose, it's ok because you can blame yourself and work harder next time, but when you lose in this game it's all the more frustrating since you know someone else who played exactly the same way could have won.

RATING: 8
Very challenging co-op game.  You are four kung-fu martial artists defending the town against a horde of ghosts and ghoulies.  Each player has a special power.  Each ghost has a special power.  Each tile of the town has a special power.  Each turn you have to choose which action to use or which ghost to beat up on (by throwing dice).  Never enough people, always on the edge of defeat.  You're trying to last long enough for the boss man to come out so you can defeat him.  Very challenging!  Susceptible to dominant player syndrome though.  If one player is much more experienced or assertive, can start just telling everyone what to do as no one has any secret knowledge (like no cards).  Otherwise, good fun!

2014-04-24

After more plays, I like Ghost Stories less and less. I only enjoy the game if I play it with the right game (funny) group. Nowadays I found the decisions somewhat obvious so luck (cards and dice) is the main determining factor in victory or failure.

Ghost Stories feels very repetitive and the gameplay is long for what the game offers.

I think this can be a better 1 player game as turns would be so quickly and downtime will be zero. I will try it this way soon on the iPad to see if I’m missing something. 

The art is great though. There are lots of better CoOp games out there (Arkham Horror, Robinson Crusoe, Sentinels of the Multiverse).

RATING: 9
My very first impression with this game was a bit disappointing one. I took a glimpse at the box cover art, and I cannot help but look the other way. I understand that many like this kind of art-style, but for myself, it was simply weird. It took me many months before I decided to pick up my copy after receiving many recommendations from others to try this one out.

The components were amazing out of the box. Ghost and Taoist miniatures, and thick tiles alone were enough to impress me. And the arts found on cards were actually pretty well done! It seemed like there were two different artist worked on this game - one for box art and other just for cards. 

Each taoists' special ability combined with villagers to drive off waves of ghosts were very awesome. Especially if you have watched any of old Chinese ghost stories films from 80~90s, you can really immerse yourself into the theme. 

I tried this game at introductory level by myself, and barely beat it out of 5 tries. Until I can get the mechanics down, and come up with a strategy, this is going to stay on my table for a long time.

RATING: 9
I normally hate "optimization" games since they feel more like a puzzle; but this is so well cloaked in theme, and asks you to choose among so many options each turn that I am drawn in. (Some of that, I admit, is a preference for "sticky-rice to exorcise hopping vampires" in comparison to "potions to kill dragons, elves, and hobbits".) What makes GS for me is the constant level of tension, the large amount of luck (which mitigates the 'imitate-a-robot-and-compute' typical of efficiency game), and the random set-up which make each game feel different. Love the haunter mechanic (tiles flip over as they get haunted every couple turns). This game feels and looks unique--rare these days. Big plus is it can be played both solo or two player in [i]two[/i] different ways (with neutral boards, or each player playing several ghosts). I find myself not pulling it out cause of the set-up time--people complain about Arkham Horror but this is worse per game length.

RATING: 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A relentless onslaught of ghosts that quickly turns into a downward spiral qi-less hell!!  It will be satisfying when we win this game. One day...

This is a good, difficult co-op. While co-ops are not my favorite, my fiance loves them and so I'm starting to enjoy them more as well. Funny that. 

Features of this co-op that my be attractive or un-attractive depending on your taste. 

- It is extremely difficult and will take a number of plays to find winning strategies. I do believe experience will pay off, though.

- It is very fighty with lots of dice-rolls. There are ways to reduce the impact of luck, but it is still there and a few bad rolls in a row can be difficult to recover from. I would guess a good strategy would include setting yourself up so that you are less dependent on great rolls to win.

- The tension the game creates is palpable. You feel like you are on the edge of disaster throughout and you will find yourself often in a position where there are numerous options and none of them good enough.

- The turns are quite repetitive. I think the short play time and constant tension mitigate this potential weakness, but it is there.

With 7 Wonders, Ghost Stories, Hanabi and Takenoko, Bauza is quietly proving to be a top-flight designer of mid-weight games. His games are all quite different from each other, but all good, which shows that his is a designer with plenty of ideas and staying power.

RATING: 2
Just awful.  The art is there, though campy (which isnt really my thing), the challenge is insane, and I just don't find it any fun at all.

I don't care for games that just beat you down every turn (same problem with Pandemic to, perhaps, a lesser degree).  I'm fine with a dash or even a helping of risk and crisis management (i.e. Downfall of Pompeii, Great Fire of London, etc..) but when the game's premise is extreme crisis management, where the goal is just to survive one more round with the hopes that the card draw will be favorable enough for you to mitigate enough each turn to survive, I just find that it lacks any sort of fun element and becomes more fatalistic than anything else.  

I know this is very low, but after having played this 3 times and having a similar disastrous experience with it each time, I'm committed to this rating.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
n Ghost Stories, players are ninjas slaying all manner of evil spirits as they attempt to take over a palace. And they just keep coming...

...and coming, and coming. You know the famous scene in Rambo III when Stallone unloads with the M60, sweeping from side to side, felling dozens of Soviet soldiers in slow motion? Well, that's basically what this game is but with players rolling dice against a thick deck of baddies. There's some depth here, to be sure, but virtually every option and maneuver is spent either rolling dice or ensuring that a future roll will succeed. Roll dem bones. Autobots, roll out. Let's roll.

:zombie:

I don't really have the stamina for it. It reminds me of my old college roommate who would watch hours of Dragonball Z. You know how those guys go all Super Saiyan, pumping out gutteral war-cries while their hair blazes and the camera cuts back and forth?

Yeah, that's Ghost Stories.

RATING: 10

RATING: 8
No game puts me on the edge of my seat like Ghost Stories. Fighting the good fight has never been so tense, and I love the way that I have all of the townspeople by my side. The ghosts are challenging, and there's no sense of relief stronger than getting a ghost you know you can handle. The difficulty is what sets it apart. Yes, every cooperative game changes things up enough to feel like you aren't playing the exact same game, but Ghost Stories is on a different level. The way that you're working through the deck of ghosts in whatever ordered you shuffled along with a boss that is one of ten possibilities feels fresher than any other! I just wish that it came with a different deck of ghosts to use without having to buy an expansion that changes the core gameplay too much. 

That all being said,there needs to be a more clear explanation in the rulebook About haunters. Haunters only move on the active players board. My wife and I lasted for like 5-10 turns the first 3 times we played because we were moving all the haunters on every turn. There is a forum about it on BGG, but we have the 2013 edition and still made that mistake. The rulebook definitely left room for confusion in many more places.(I didn't realize what you actually did on your first turn until I watched youtube videos) Please fix it because it is otherwise such a great game!

RATING: 7
A solid effort, definitely well designed, and the artwork (though not my style) is good.  Even the theme (though veering a little too close to fantasy for my tastes) is unique and more interesting than most.

Still, it's a cooperative game, and without some sort of traitor aspect I don't think a cooperative game could ever be a true favorite of mine.  Plus, Ghost Stories definitely would suffer from a "tell the other players what to do" problem when you have a more experienced, or just more bossy, players.

The game is really hard and I would imagine that it provides a good amount of satisfaction when you beat it.  I don't know how that feels yet, we still haven't won!

Įdomus kooperatinis žaidimas, kuris turėtų būti žaidžiamas su kuo nors, kas gerai moka taisykles, nes iš tiesų labai nesunku ką nors užmiršti: pavyzdžiui, ėjimo pradžioje atversti naują vaiduoklį.
