RATING: 9
Ratings upgraded to 9 after about 25 plays.  I am not a particular fan of co-op games, so I am surprised that I am addicted to this game.  I am attracted to determining the different permutations of the roles/tiles and how those affect your chances of winning.  We had problems winning the first couple of games, but thereafter, the game became much easier to win.  I am currently 1 for 2 in Hell mode (Solitaire).
  
------

It seems like the Solitaire version is the easiest to beat, though things tend to go to hell much faster.  The best role to select if you are having trouble winning are:
- middle tile: herbalist
- Green: no curse, extra die (play this taoist)
- Yellow: take tokens
- Blue: double action
Try to get lots of tokens before you go fighting (it'll only take one turn to load up to 9 tokens by doing a double herbalist and Yellow's ability).

Four player game is tougher because your tao tokens are distributed.  Your advantages are the extra Yin-Yang tokens.

Ghost Stories is a cooperative game in which the players protect the village from incarnations of the lord of hell – Wu-Feng – and his legions of ghosts before they haunt a town and recover the ashes that will allow him to return to life. Each Player represents a Taoist monk working together with the others to fight off waves of ghosts.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I like challenging cooperative games, but sadly, [b]Ghost Stories[/b]' difficulty [b][i]completely[/i][/b] broke the game for me.

I would [i][b]really[/b][/i] like to love this game, but I just can't, because of the game's insane difficulty - and we are even talking about the lowest difficulty variant here. And that's coming from someone who also enjoys the really harsh [b][thing=121921][/thing][/b], which is also not perfect because it is very swingy, but at least you have options and can plan ahead.

[b]Ghost Stories[/b] would have been really great, if there would have been exciting peaks of challenge and calm moments for regrouping and strategising the next turns.

[b]Pandemic[/b] executes this balances perfectly. [b]Ghost Stories[/b] on the other hand just keeps coming and coming at the players, making them feel like they are juggling sharp knives and need to add another one after each turn -- until the inevitable catastrophe happens. Everyone knows it, it's just a matter of time. Challenge is fun, unfairness is not.

I'm especially frustrated with this game because I really love the fresh and unique theme, the gorgeous artwork, the easy rules and the modular board - but the game completely shuts me out of the fun. :thumbsdown:

The components are overall great, but there is one big negative aspect: the colour-coded dice are not engraved, so the faces will over time wear out and become blank.

This game could have been a 7-8/10, but sadly: it just isn't.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I think this game has 1 big flaw, the dices. It's not that I hate dices in game, on the contrary, it's just that the odds are so low and each action is so important that a bad roll can cost you the game.

I suggested a variant that when you fail a roll, you get a token of the color of the ghost you wanted to banish. The goal is to reduce the effect of bad luck through the game. And possibly make a game played at easy much easier to finish with newbies.

By the way, most people say that the game is hard, but we managed to win a 4p game at easy. Still, we were working closely together and we were not so lucky. Personally, I think that newbies should have a chance to win an easy game.

From a mechanic point of view, this game could look like a puzzle. So people could find it more as a puzzle game with a very thin theme. Sure the feeling and the theme is not very deep when you play. The feeling you get during play is more close to puzzle solving.

Many people compare this game to pandemic, I could say that it is a bit true, but ghost story has something pandemic does not have: The climax. A game of pandemic ends in the middle of the "story", Here in ghost stories, the incarnations makes sure there is a climax at the end for more tension. 

The modular map is an interesting design that gives a bit of replay value. I like modular boards.

So in general, I think this game is very positive. Like I said, there might be a few changes needed to reduce the effect of bad luck. The games feels more like a puzzle where you do not get in very deep with the theme or in your character.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game is probably the hardest co-op I've played, and you will definitely feel the tension as the ghosts start to overwhelm you. Generally I feel like this game is tempo-based: it is almost guaranteed that you will fall behind on killing ghosts, the trick is just to hold off loss of tempo for long enough that come end game you can just ignore everyone but Wu Feng for one last ditch attack before you die. Although several consecutive bad rolls early game can really screw you over, I feel like this game still requires a fair deal of strategy. Great art with good components, and although the dice come sticky as someone has mentioned in the forums using peanut butter will get rid of said stickiness.

EDIT: game is much easier with fewer players. Also, while luck does play a large factor this game requires a lot more strategic positioning of the monks & ghosts, along with risk analysis than initially meets the eye. Ideally, you never want to rely on the dice, and so risk mitigation is extremely important in this game, but sometimes there is just a ghost you have to finish off without a Tao token buffer, especially with the more limited resources with more players.

You move your Taoist to fight ghosts by rolling dice or by activating powers on various locations in the village. RATING: 8.6
When I first played observing all the rules correctly (3rd time), I was effectively hammered by the game, as 3 very difficult monsters spawned at the very beggining of the game. I also lost on my second correct play, but I ALMOST won. I only lost due to a ridiculously unlucky ghost draw when I was about to kill the incarnation of Wu Feng.

I drew a ghost which brought another ghost to the table, and then I drew a ghost which kept one die for itself, leaving me with only one die (the first one had also been stolen by the incarnation) AND made me draw ANOTHER ghost. Then I drew one that prevented me from using any of my Tao tokens :(

After that, I didn't have the time to exorcise this last ghost and, then, with only 1 poor single die left, exorcise the incarnation: 1 - a previously drawn ghost cancelled the red monk's power and 2 - I had a haunted tile. When I exorcized the Tao token ghost, the curse die haunted another tile and, before I could reach the incarnation, 2 haunters haunted 2 more village tiles.

As people can realize by reading what is written above, this is a very thematic, tense and hard cooperative game, and it just feels awesome when an applied tactic works against the board.

Plus, the art is neat and the setup time is short.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Solitaire: Holy shit, this game. THIS GAME. The first day I got a chance to play it, I played it 10 times. I've never done that with any other game.

I had concerns about it after reading many reviews -- too random, too little feeling of progress, "Yahtzee with ghosts," etc. None of that was an issue for me. Sure, there's randomness: I've lost on a single die roll -- but that comes down to poor planning on my part more than simple chance. It's a puzzle, one with lots of pieces and things to tweak and never enough time to do all of it, and it's brilliant. And it looks great, with lots of color and a fantastic art style.

Solitaire is very well implemented. Apart from the useless cemetery, nothing about it feels off. It's a blast to play. Some village configurations make life more difficult, as do (of course) some draws and some powers. Everything matters, but it can all be worked around, and I learned something new in all of my first games.

Out of my first 10 plays on the lowest difficulty, I won 4 times (best score 26) and lost 6 times (worst score -39), a pleasant balance in my book. More importantly, I had fun losing. For a game notorious for its difficulty level, that's a good thing.

It's brutal and unrelenting in its pace at times, and it's rare that there's much breathing room -- a turn, maybe two if you're lucky. There are occasional easy choices, but sometimes I see later on that they seemed like easy choices but impacted the game in unexpected ways. Almost every turn involves a tough decision, but the option set is truncated sharply by the game state; that adds up to about a 30-45 minute solo game for me, which is a great timeframe.

Sitting here writing this comment on that same first day, I want to play it again right now. It's gotten its hooks into my brain with its perfect mix of challenge, luck, puzzle, and superb artwork and theme. 

It's not all roses, though. The rulebook is one of the worst I've seen, I suspect due to poor translation. BGG makes answering questions easy enough during play, but every other game or so I've discovered I'd been doing something slightly wrong or had missed a rule that got slipped in somewhere unexpected.

The components are also a mixed bag: gorgeous, but not all high-quality. The boards, minis, and tokens are all excellent, and look like they'll hold up well. The cards are thin, glossy, cheap-feeling, and show visible wear after a few plays. (I don't care, so unsleeved they'll stay.) And the dice -- yikes. Screened, not etched, and after a couple games the spots became sticky. For $50 MSRP that's a shame.

But. But! The game itself is so good that I don't care about the clunky rulebook or the mix of great/poor components. Maybe I should, but I'm too busy having fun to worry about it.

Ghost Stories is one of the most satisfying and enjoyable games I've ever played.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Elegant cooperative game. Everything fits together seamlessly. It's also quite atmospheric. You could argue that the gameplay (drawing of cards) is somewhat repetitive. But, I think you have quite a bit to chew on between draws, which makes up for the repetition. It's true that this game is HARD! I don't care how many games you've played or how intelligent you are, this game will always be tough to beat your first time. Interestingly, some of the special powers that seem more helpful at first glance are actually less helpful in retrospect. The game is always going to come down to the dice rolls. If you roll poorly, you cannot win. If you roll average, the odds are stacked against you. If you roll well, it's still not an easy game. The dice also make it a different game than something like Pandemic, because your are not just working against the cards, but the dice as well. Excellent game. I can see why it's so popular. 

Update 5/22/15: Unfortunately, the second time I played this game, I had to almost completely re-learn the rules. It's a very process-driven game, not a big idea game, so the ruleset can definitely escape you. It took about almost an hour to get through them. Once we started playing, we were more focused on playing the correct rules than enjoying the experience. Bottom line: this is a game you need to play multiple times and within a reasonable time frame to truly enjoy. That doesn't really fit into my wheelhouse, but I like the gameplay and the components enough to keep it around. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
3 / 5 - Good.

There's a lot to like about Ghost Stories. The theme comes across well, partly thanks to the evocative and brilliantly done artwork, there's plenty of strategy to think about, a tough learning curve, plenty of variability and an interesting solo game. However I didn't find there was *quite* enough variation on hand to entirely kill the alpha-player problem that so dogs co-op games. I was also annoyed at the way the random incarnation can show up and totally torpedo your otherwise cunningly-played game just because it happens to be one of the more difficult ones.

RATING: 10
Best game of 2008 and one of my top10 favorites.
The best co-op game. One of the best games in general.. It's by Bauza, probably the best designer there is too. Ghost Stories has perfect mix of Pandemic type of serious planning and then less serious dice-throwing that ultimately decides your faith. In other words perfect mix of strategy and luck. Cool components and theme (it's folklore so both fantasy and non-fantasy fans can enjoy it, I'm immersed at least). Rulebook could be bit better but the rules itself are simple. But it's still very challenging game, which is great because nothing is less replayable than easy co-op game. AND it has different difficulty levels, and then when you think you're done it even has very good expansion (White Moon) that brings it to next level that you'll probably never tire of. All the smaller promo expansions are very good too. Yeah, it's the best co-op game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
Game in a Nutshell:  Play as Monks fighting off ghosts with the help of villagers that are threatening your small village.

Played as:  2,4 player

Pros:  Has a fun theme that should appeal to most anyone. Very nice artwork on all the tiles and cards. The plastic bits are excellent, especially the ghosts who lean over the threatened tiles as if to swallow them up.

Cons:  The game has enough niggly little rules to remember, as is. But to have a terrible rule book that offers messy (at best) to non-existent clarification is a substantial set-back in the accessibility of the game.  There’s something strangely unnatural about the flow of play, or maybe that’s just an extension of the poor rules clarification and lack of a good player-aid. The board layout is too abstract for my tastes, offering little connection to what’s happening on the table. It just looks like a jumbled mess of cardboard and plastic.  After only a couple games, I’m not sure where the variety is going to come from going forward (sans money-grab expansions)... the modular board is too small to really mix anything up and the ghosts are like the Taco Bell menu: same five ingredients, just layered in a different order. Overall, I found there to be a lot of the same-same, with no visual connection, and a surprising lack of real excitement.

Other:  Maybe I’ve been lucky in my limited play experience, but I’ve found the game to be much easier than advertised.  I think a few straight-forward strategies can take players a long way.  I won’t say that’s a con yet until I’ve played a few more times. Also, it’s worth noting, I have spent far too much time making sure I’ve got the rules right and haven’t found any major mistakes.

Best Use:  If you’re a co-op nut and you’ve burned out on all your other options already.

RATING: 5

RATING: 8
Board Game Warriors - traded Diplomacy + $20

This game is strange to me.  I can't decide whether I really like it, or only sort of like it.

It's not easy to pick up and play, and it's not an easy game to teach to new people and then enjoy.  You need to play a few games before everyone really "gets it" and can make sound decisions on their own.

I am slightly embarrassed to admit that I have played the solo game, and less embarrassed to say that it actually works pretty well.  I lost the first time 5 minutes in, but won the second time after only about 30 minutes.  And it was more entertaining then a game of card solitaire.

I wouldn't recommend this to anyone who doesn't play "advanced" games.  It's not easy to learn, it's not easy to pick up and start playing.  It needs a real time investment to be enjoyable.  And I have yet to see if the invested time is really worth the effort.

RATING: 8
I am not convinced that this game can be defeated. Nonetheless, it is rather a hoot to watch one's imminent defeat unveil itself with the turn of a single card.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Finally brought this to the table. Very, very addictive. We got a couple of important rules wrong (and so the game was a little too easy, even for the introductory difficulty) but these will be fixed in the next game. 

Exorcising ghosts is immensely satisfying, and the encourages teamwork, but doesn't completely depend on it, meaning the game doesn't appear to suffer as much from the same problem as other cooperative titles: that is, that someone can take charge. 

The game offers tense gameplay, and although it was somewhat easy in our incorrect-rule introductory session, it's clear this is going to be a hard slog on the higher difficulty levels. The battle with Wu-Feng seemed a little too easy at the end, however this may be due to the aforementioned rule confusion. The concept is brilliant though: the major boss battle combined with a simple game-driven time limit makes for a very climactic end to the game.

Just a note though: whatever you do, download the one-page reference sheet from the Ghost Stories files on BGG. Sharing one copy of the quick-reference and handbook manuals included with the game would have been a nightmare considering all the various icons and player/villager/enemy powers.

All in all, even with casual gamers (including my girlfriend, who is fairly picky when it comes to thematic games), all 4 players were thoroughly entertained and eager to play it again. A sign of a truly great game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
[microbadge=1714]  [microbadge=21390]

14-Oct-2016:  A couple of quick comments about White Moon:
•  It definitely takes the edge off the base game's notorious difficulty.
•  It also adds to the game's fiddliness for both setup and gameplay but not to the point where I found it annoying. 
•  This is an easy recommend, especially if you feel like the base game is just a bit too mean.  Not a necessity but an expansion that adds a lot of additional options for the player.

17-Feb-2013:  This is an excellent, and tough, cooperative game where you are a group of Taoist monks fighting off a (seemingly) never ending onslaught of ghosts. These evil beings are sent from the depths of the Underworld by the banished Wu Feng. Using various powers and help from the Villagers, the monks, if they survive long enough, will have to fight one of the reincarnations of Wu Feng (the "big bad") to win the game.

This is a tactics heavy game. You will need to deal with a constant barrage of ghosts being added to the board, each with their set of powers and actions. It is almost kin to a tower defense game as at least one ghost will be added on every monk's turn. You will have to exorcise them by using dice and special tokens, matching the varying strengths of the ghosts.

The randomness of set up, differing abilities, what ghosts and what order they come out during play, and which incarnation (or incarnations at higher difficulty levels) of Wu Feng you must defeat add to the replayability and my enjoyment of this one. The artwork is very good. The theme is unique. The quality of all of the tiles and chits are great. The only minor complaint I have with the components is the quality of the cards. They're pretty poor, but you do only shuffle them prior to gameplay and that's all, so it shouldn't be a problem in the long run.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.75
My wife & I don't play cooperative games often -- and Pandemic has accounted for all but 1 of our coop game plays -- so we don't have much to compare against Ghost Stories. Relative to Pandemic, I liked all of the different player powers and villager tile powers in Ghost Stories -- it led to many instances where we'd come up with several different options that we'd need to choose from. I felt that kind of situation occurred more than it does when we play Pandemic, and I enjoy that kind of thinking.

On the other hand, I like that it's easier to plan ahead in Pandemic because you know you'll see the same cities cycling through after an epidemic. With Ghost Stories, however, you never know what's coming so all you can do is constantly react. So while we enjoyed the game, I'm not sure yet whether it's a keeper.

RATING: 9
Excellent game that I love to play, despite being a frequent hater of cooperative games. 

Ghost Stories manages to eliminate the Alpha Gamer problem that can plague these games by ensuring that there are almost always at least two (and sometimes three or four) equally viable moves to make. 

You really feel like you're part of a team of Taoist warriors, desperately trying to beat back the ghostly hordes from a small rural village in ancient China. 

The artwork and production values are a step above. A lot of hard decisions and twists of fate packed into a game that plays in an hour (or less if you get defeated). 

I usually don't enjoy solo games, either, but you can have a good time with one player in Ghost Stories. I have no doubt I'll spend many more hours on this one. 

Damn you, Wu Feng!!!

Played: About 24 times, including half a dozen solo games.

UPDATE: Bumping up from an 8 to a 9 after further play. This may change down the road, but right now I always want to play this game. I really enjoy how brutally difficult this is along with the hard choices you are presented with in every game. Never thought I would rate a cooperative game this high.

RATING: 3
On first contact, Ghost Stories looks and sounds lovely. After understanding its premise, you're probably quite interested in playing it, provided you have survived the poorly laid out rulebook. The only tiny problem is that, how shall I put it... the balance is all over the place, in a really hardcore way. The only time I ever won included all the following:

    We played on the tutorial difficulty.
    We were not at max player count. (The game scales horribly and most players claiming to have a nice win rate probably play solo rather than 4 players.)
    We chose our monk powers. (Some of them are almost strictly worse than their alternative.)
    We got really nice ghost draws in early game and haunters were spaced out.
    We drew the easiest-to-beat incarnation of Wu Feng.
    We got a rule wrong, resulting in a player losing 8 less Qi over the course of the game than he should have. (For the uninitiated, that means we should have lost horribly.)

Perhaps there are some arcane strategic choices that we're unable to see, but as far as I'm concerned, Ghost Stories only understands that players dislike cooperative games that are beaten too easily; therefore it absolutely ensures that you will get wrecked over and over and over again, only able to win with the conjunction of near-optimal play and a statistically abnormal amount of luck. I'm not that masochistic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
In this 1-4 player cooperative game, players are a Taoist, combating Chinese ghosts. Each turn, a player draws a ghost card, and places it. There are 9 villages where players can enlist help, such as grabbing tokens to defeat ghosts, or automatically killing ghosts at a cost of a life. Players can also wander adjacent to ghosts and roll dice to attempt to kill the ghosts. Players win by killing a Wu Feng ghost (a top tier ghost), and the ghosts win by hanuting a number of villages or killing off the Taoists. There are four difficulty levels (Initiation, Normal, Nightmare, Hell), which handicaps the life tokens players start with or the number of Wu Feng ghosts they have to kill to win.

This is a difficult but very fun, and engaging game, but I like the idea that it is difficult to win, since it is challenging.

As a strategy tip, we found making the blue player go first so they can use a double action on the buddha square, or the square to get two tokens works well, then have another player go to the square to put on a permanent token of a color.

Yes, the rules don't take care of the myriad of special cases that can arise, but the designer is making an effort to answer them here.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a very keenly designed and unexpectedly abstract co-op game, with a wonderful and original (if slightly shallowly attached) theme laid on top, which was my initial draw towards it. It is very tactical and requires a great deal of attention in terms of what moves and actions each player can afford to play and when, since it is very unforgiving of mistakes or poor dice rolling.

However, as beautiful and intriguing as the game is I am not yet convinced of its longevity when compared to other co-op games such as Arkham Horror, partially due to the more abstract nature of the gameplay and partly because I do like longer games. If it does stand the test of time along with my other solo/co-op games, (or if you prefer shorter games in general) then this game should definitely get a 9 instead of an 8 though. 

But it loses a big point because the rulebook (at least in the first printing) is horrid. Poorly laid out and full of information that is either not clear enough, mis-directing in its examples, or plain mis-translated. It requires copious amounts of time reading FAQs and rules postings in order to actually play "correctly", and for such a mechanically simple game this makes for a lot of unneeded frustration.

Still, after getting past the problems it is addictive, very clever and great to look at, and regardless of its lifespan I am already getting my money's worth in sheer enjoyment.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
A household favourite thanks to my brother for getting my husband and I hooked on it one summer. We love that it has the cooperative intensity of Arkham Horror, but without the 4 hour gameplay and 20 minute setup. 

Our Rating Guide (1 = Disappointed, 3=hit&miss, 5= Owned it!)

1. Originality - 5 - Taoist Monks who use magical superpowers to save villages from evil ghosts. Enough said!  

2. Artwork - 5 - The cards are all unique and beautifully terrifying. The tiles are classy. The game pieces are functional.

3. Quality of Contents - 5 - For how often we've played, this game pulls through. Yes, there's some wear on the card edges, but overall I'm not worried that I'll miss out on teaching my grandchildren how to play. Yeah, I want to be that grandma - screw you cribbage!

4. Storyline - 5- Again, Taoist Monks who use magical superpowers to save villages from evil ghosts. Enough said!  

5. Playthrough - 5- Even when this game kicks my butt mercilessly, the first words out of my mouth are "again!" The rule book can be a bit frustrating, but once you get all of the symbols figured out, you won't need to go back to it again because really all of the details are in the game play.

6. Instructions - 3 - it's like reading an IKEA manual. 

7. Replayability - 5 - again and again and again!
	
8. Two player - 5 - Usually it's just my husband and I, or me teaching another person. It almost works better because you can use power tokens that let you use non-playing characters' powers.

9. Large Group 4 player max - not for a crowd.

10. Fun Factor - 5 - again and again and again!

RATING: 6
ABSOLUTELY BRUTAL co-op game that will either reinforce or completely negate your opinions on co-op games, depending on what you've played before.  You simply have no choice but to co-operate if you plan to have ANY chance of defeating this game.  Simply put, so much can go so horribly wrong so horribly quickly -- I seriously believe that there are games that are guaranteed losses, based on the luck of the deck.  How well you do depends on how much you can depend on things that aren't dice, time is definitely not on your side, and even the BEGINNER'S level of this game will make you sweat if you don't understand the importance of each and every gear in motion.

I have owned this game for close to 5 years, I have played it several times during that period, and I have beaten Wu-Feng exactly one time.

The primary issue is, due to its incredible difficulty, the "dominant player" syndrome comes out even stronger in this one.  There's room for maybe 3 sub-optimal moves in Ghost Stories and dominant players are going to pipe up every time a move is made.

RATING: 8
First impression (3 players): It's a cooperation game with a ghost theme. Your task is it banish incarnation of a powerful spirit but before you can do that you must stay alive until he'll appear. On the plus side the game isn't too easy (it might be too hard actually..). The struggling is half a game. If this would be too easy it wouldn't be as fun. 

Ghost Stories suffers from the cooperation game basic problem: One (experienced) player can play the game by himself if needed. There is no hidden information. Also basic gameplay might became repetetive and a bit mechanical after a few plays. Game works well with 3 players but it's best when played with full 4 players. Four might be the sweet spot for difficulty too.

The game is sadistically hard. It is hard even with easiest difficulty level. I don't know what it tells about me but I want to play more! Not sure how long-lived Ghost Stories will be but it has been enormously fun to play so far.

Update (24.1.2010) : The game is hard. 7 games now and no victory for heroes (easiest level of difficulty). Also me and the rules for the game are incompatible as I'm always getting at least one tiny rule wrong when playing. This is partly because I don't own the game and playing someone else's copy so there hasn't been any quick reference / faq printed along like in my games.

RATING: 7
En voilà un bon jeu de coopération qui ne paye pas de mine.
Le thème me plait beaucoup et les illustrations sont de toute beauté.
Le propre des jeux en coopératif est qu'ils peuvent être joués soit en solo ou à plusieurs. Pour le coup, ce n'est pas très arrangeant de jouer seul à Ghost Stories : les plateaux des autres joueurs absents sont "neutres" et sont accessibles par le jeu mais surtout par les fantômes. Pour moi je trouve que cela créé un déséquilibre par toujours facile à jauger ou à réquilibrer par le paquet de cartes fantôme à gérer.
Plateau général de jeu est original et bien pensé. Sauf un ou deux villageois qui me semblent pas vraiment indispensables, le reste des villageois est bien pensé.
On prend du plaisir à gérer l'urgence de ces fantômes hanteurs qui arrivent de toute part.
Il y a pas mal de jets de dés : le systèmes d'objets à sacrifier pour les plus handicapés du dé d'entre nous est bien pensé.
Le matériel est impeccable, que ce soit les figurines, les cartes "glassées", les tuiles et les marqueurs.
De façon générale j'ai bien aimé y jouer mais il me semble qu'on commence à bien rigoler à partir de 3 joueurs.

RATING: 7.75
Oh boy...this one is strangely addictive! I thought Pandemic was a very difficult game to beat! I thought that some of the GOO's and situations in Arkham really made Arkham Horror difficult to beat! And now...this! Ghost Stories is really difficult to beat...no doubt about it! 

The game is relatively simple...kill the deadly monsters or be killed! I like this game because it is somewhat fresh in mechanics, nice design-artwork-components, and it has a fairly steady stream of game play! The strategy of when to use Chi and Ying/Yang is extremely important to your survival. Collecting tao tokens and Buddhas...when there is time...is most difficult...but essential! Tricky game of timing, luck, group strategy, and...yes...survival!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
心得:
腳色能力差異略大
如果沒有使用四個人
有些腳色能力相對較廢會增加難度
遊戲主要策略點在移動鬼使得可以一次驅逐兩隻才划算

規則:
*鬼牌的左下是進場效果，中間是每回合效果，右下是離場效果，左上是生命，右上是顏色
*隨機擺置中央成為3x3的村莊版圖，另外四塊圖版隨機放置上下左右，隨機玩家顏色跟能力(對應圖版面)，每個玩家拿四氣(沒有上限)跟1個陰陽標記，1個自己顏色跟1個黑色的道標記，所有棋子放在中央村莊，兩個玉佛標記放在對應村莊
*魔王卡10抽1，放在鬼怪卡最下面10張上(45鬼怪-1魔王-10鬼怪)
*由最近看過功夫片的起始，每個玩家輪流動作，一次有兩階段
A.陰階段
1.主動玩家的圖板上鬼怪使用中間能力
>鬧鬼: 卡上前進一格，在圖板上則對應村莊鬧鬼，板塊翻面，鬼怪放回卡上，效果直達整行
>鬼骰: 扔骰看結果 直接村莊鬧鬼/抽一張鬼牌/該玩家棄光所有道標記/該玩家失去1氣
2.如果該玩家圖版有3隻鬼，則該玩家失去1氣並跳過抽鬼階段
3.抽一張鬼牌，紅綠藍黃鬼到對應顏色玩家圖版，黑色則直接到主動玩家圖版，如果滿了就隨意放，並啟動左下效果，如果全部12格都滿還要補鬼時主動玩家失去1氣
B.陽階段
1.移動一步 可對腳 可不動
2.村莊能力或驅跟該村莊相鄰的鬼 ，驅鬼擲三顆色骰，必須擲出對應鬼耐力的顏色骰才成功(白面是百搭)，可用道標記補足，邊角處可一次驅逐兩隻，可使用同村莊的其他人道標記
3.之前回合有的話可放玉佛在沒鬼的位置，邊緣可一次放兩個，當鬼要到該塊時直接移除遊戲，卡片上效果無視，玉佛則放回村莊
*陰陽標記隨時可用 使用其他格的村莊能力或是把鬧鬼村莊復原，用完就翻面蓋著只能藉由某些鬼的獎勵拿回
*沒氣的玩家掛點放在祭壇村莊上，棄掉所有他的物品，可被其他人復活，且該玩家的陰階段1跟2還是會執行
*魔王牌視為一個鬼牌放在對應顏色位置，要完全符合條件才能驅逐並獲勝，且不受巫術小屋跟玉佛影響，如果有玉佛直接擺回原村莊，每張打爆都會獲得1氣1陰陽標記並可決定誰拿
*勝利條件驅逐魔王牌，失敗條件 全掛/三個村莊鬧鬼/最後一張鬼牌抽出
*難度調整可每人起始5氣
***道士能力***
*黃 1.移動前可放標記在任何鬼上降1防禦力，多色的可在擲骰後決定降哪一個 2.移動前可拿任意一種顏色的道標記
*紅 1.移動前可移動隊友一步 2.可移動到任意格
*藍 1.可做兩次村莊或兩次驅鬼行動 2. 可做一次村莊和一次驅鬼行動
*綠 1.驅鬼可多擲一顆骰，且永不擲詛咒骰 2.可重擲骰一次或重擲詛咒骰
***1~3人規則****
*2~3人時，沒有玩家的版圖放3氣，每個玩家多拿一個力量標記，兩人是要在對面，2/3人時移除10/5張鬼牌
*Solo 移除15張鬼牌，各色標記各一，起始難度在多1黑，拿3個力量標記
*使用力量標記可使用中立板圖的道師能力，使用後標記放在中間村莊，踩到中央時可拿回手，死掉也會把力量標記放中間
*中立板圖會執行陰的前兩個階段，抽鬼牌階段不會執行，且氣消失補不回來，如果沒氣就不能使用該版圖能力，之後掉氣要選擇任一玩家掉
**難度**
*普通  起始3氣，且沒有黑色標記
*噩夢 起始跟普通一樣，增加魔王卡，1~2人使用3張，3~4人使用4張(牌庫底開始每10張插1張)
*地獄 跟惡夢一樣，起始沒有陰陽標記

RATING: 8

But no one can keep track of all the player's special abilities or the villager's powers so it takes the full compliment of your team to solve the puzzle of eliminating ghosts from your village. The rulebook isn't intuitive but Ghost Stories is a better game played than studied. Great artwork, great components, this is a good game to end the day of competitive Euros and 4x games.

RATING: 8
Half a dozen plays in and we're trying to crack Nightmare level. It's pure co-op, so really it's all about trying to determine the ultimate strategy for the board you're faced with, and then executing it with luck. The challenge is ... how best to place ghosts to allow you to take advantage of village actions as often as possible whilst keeping the ghosts under control. Not for everyone, but we've enjoyed the "what could we do better next time" post-mortems. The lack of a traitor means it's purely an exercise though.

RATING: 6
To win you pretty much can't make a single non-optimal move. During 95% of your turns, you will be trying to prevent an immediate danger/ risk. Because of this dynamic you almost never get to do ANY planning ahead, you are just constantly responding the highest priority risk. I feel this is the major setback for this game, which is otherwise a lot of fun. There is some puzzling to figure out, but often the highest priority risk makes for straight forward decision making.  Also, I feel it becomes substantially easier with fewer players as you can just keep re-taking the power token thingos from the center tile. The fewer players, the more tokens that can be utilised in this way. I don't get all the 'its to hard' comments though. It's very easy to find many ways to adjust the difficulty if players decide they need to.

RATING: 7
A cooperative game is alwasy welcome. They just tend to be quite hard. This game is especially hard.
Well, it didn't help that different rules were controversial and we played many things wrong. The character abilities are also quite uneven.

Ghost Stories is a thrilling and difficult game. Slowly the town becomes hopelessly overwhelmed by the ghosts and you wish for a rematch. The dice sure look nifty and probably it was us but they never give the result you need!

Oh yeah, and the theme! The ancient chinese mythology is a lot more appealing than any modern stuff would be. It gives the game a slightly noble touch.

This is a four-player game, don't try with less players. You will only be sweating and cursing those ghosts, even more than they curse you...

RATING: 10

Great game. Simply love it. Mechanism of the game perfectly matches the theme so that you really have the feel of the ghosts attacking the village from every possible direction and the group of brave taoist doing whatever they can to stop them.

Game is very challenging, no to say hard. Although we were lucky in first two games and considered the game of being too easy (we have read the rules correctly), the third and further games showed us we were so wrong...

Big advantage of the game are the four difficulty levels and option for one up to four players. It is quite expensive but there are tones of components you are getting in this price. Cards, miniatures, board tiles, tokens, etc. Everything beautifully ilustrated, especially the cards (each unique, even if some monsters are doubled each has unique illustration, what is rare).

There is a lot of randomness in the game but this is a must in cooperation games to differ each gameplay.

There are also few interesting extensions to boost the game and i'll definately get them all:)

RATING: 8.5
Very tough co-op game, which can even be played solo. It is quite scalable to suit your ability (although even the lowest difficulty level isn't exactly easy!).

Kind of feels like a puzzle more than a game, but it's a puzzle that randomly evolves as you play through card draws & die rolls, so this keeps the interest level high. If the game had less hidden information it could be overwhelming by requiring you to calculate too many possibilites for future moves.

During play, there is a constant struggle against the endless stream of ghosts appearing around the board. It seems that there is little room for error, with bad moves or unlucky rolls quickly accumulating until you simply can't hold them back any longer!

I really like the theme and how it has been carried through the components, although I guess it's the sort of game that could have pretty much any theme applied.

WARNING: Rules as printed are awful - even the newer downloadable ones still have various minor errors. The game isn't as complex as they make it appear however, and there is a really good "unofficial" FAQ list which is basically a compilation of official answers from the designer - that clears up pretty much everything.

The box is ridiculously over-sized, but components are good.

RATING: 9.25
This is how you make a co-operative game hard, whilst still retaining the feeling that the decisions you make strongly affect how the game develops. There is an element of randomness in whether you succeed in exorcising ghosts, due to the use of dice, but it usually feels as though it's a calculated risk. Gameplay is fast and the sense of barely keeping the village from being overrun really ramps up the tension whilst offering you countless ways to respond to the crisis at hand. If you're a fan of co-op games, this is a must-play.

Bon jeu coopératif. Le matériel est superbe, spécialement le graphiques des tuiles et cartes. La mécanique du jeu est simple, par contre, les règles sont si mal expliquées quelles rende celle-ci compliquée. Le livre de jeu ne couvre pas tous les points du jeu laissant des zones grises. Le ''sweet spot'' du jeu est de 4 joueurs et le moins de joueurs il y a, moins le jeu semble adapté et balançé. Selon mon opinion, la variante solo devrait être retestée et modifiée car il y a un petit je ne sais quoi qui semble donner l'impression que cette variante est brisée.

RATING: 6
If you like coop games (or solitaire games), this is a great one.  I personally like the theme of chinese ghost hunters, and it is very easy to get sucked into the "story".  Unlike a coop game like Arkham Horror or Touch of Evil, though, the mechanics have an abstract feel to them. This is similar to how I feel about the excellent Lord of Rings coop game and it doesn't really get in the way of enjoying the theme. Also like LotR, I think this game has excellent potential to appeal equally to the Eurogamer and Ameritrash fan (I am more of the latter).  After a few games, the game seems to be VERY tough to beat...which should be refreshing to those who don't think a coop game should be too easy to beat.  With multiple levels of difficulty, it is easy to play according to your experience/skill with the game.  The play is fresh and does not overlap with other coop games.  Solitaire potential is excellent, as you can either play solo or controlling all characters.  I love it!

RATING: 7.5
want to play - looks amazing, and an almost-sure thing for Kelly and me.
(after playing once) Yep - this is almost a sure-thing for Kel, except for the way-too-hard difficulty level.
I don't know why the designers nailed the art and theme, and then didn't follow Pandemic's example of having a beginner difficulty level that will lead to success for the players the majority of the time. You can always make something tougher, once the players have played and succeeded once.
Throw in the ridiculously-fiddly and hard-to-remember rules and you've got an almost-guaranteed-to-alienate-newbies game.
The game really almost requires an expert rules moderator, and many groups don't have that (further narrowing this game's audience).
It's too bad - I liked the game, the genre, the art and theme, and many of the mechanics - just not the difficulty level.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
A very tough and punishing co-op game that offers many levels of difficulty for players. Art is very well done but the game leans heavily on icons so expect the first couple games to take awhile as you will keep referring to the rulebook or reference sheet for help on different spirits and village tiles. Game requires strong communication among players and each player board has two sides allowing for a bit of variance in the different player powers.

The game definitely gets tense as you inch closer and closer to victory and sometimes some bad rolls will ruin it for you despite any well made plans and strategies your group has decided on. Plays best with four and it is better for someone to control multiple characters instead of following the special rules in my opinion. Regardless, always an enjoyable experience, win or lose.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Ghost Stories is hard. Some people might say it's too hard.  I generally don't like games that seem impossible.  But there is something interesting about Ghost Stories.  The theme is very intriguing and the components are gorgeous and add a lot to my overall perception of the game play.  I'm not sure if one play is enough to get a full understanding of what I like and don't like, but I'll be back after I play it a few more times.

The components are gorgeous and they feel really good.  They are smooth.  It's seems like a strange thing to remark, but I found the smoothness of the chits very striking.

(Also, the game smells really good.)

RATING: 6.5
I played Ghost Stories several times at BGG Con '08.  Most of the games I played were just so-so, but the last game I played was a incredibly rewarding and fun experience.  One of the problems is that this game has easily one of the worst rulebooks I have ever seen. RATING: 8
Component Quality:
Production values are top notch here, with very sturdy village tiles, player boards and minis. I especially love that they went with actual minis for the haunters.

Gameplay:
A very challenging strategy game. Lots of different difficulty levels and ways to set up the village makes for a ton of replay value. There's luck involved, but plenty of player actions can mitigate the luck, making Ghost Stories very much a game of strategy and skill. After many plays, certain strategies have become obvious, but dice can always make any plan more difficult.

RATING: 8.5
An exercise in self-flagellation. Great theme, artwork, and components. Simple but fun mechanics that make for an incredibly challenging co-op or solitaire game. A seemingly endless flow of ghosts are introduced (with powers that kick in upon introduction, each round, or upon exorcism). The players, "Taoists," move about the village soliciting help from the villagers (gaining Tao tokens, resurrecting fallen comrades, etc.) and rolling dice to exorcise the ghosts in a tactical tug-of-war. Achieved first victory in game #25.

RATING: 5.6
There is an excellent line towards the end of The Eagle has Landed, in which the German officer says 'The time has come when I no longer control events, events control me'. And that is the problem with this game, you don't really take a pro-active role, you simply firefight.

Ghost Stories is a co-operative game about Power Rangers fighting Rubber Monsters (Okay, its Taoist monks and Ghosts, but frankly its a flimsy theme). Ultimately players must hold off the rubber monsters long enough for the big baddy to arrive and then defeat him. The basic structure will be familiar to all players of co-operative games, each player draws a new ghost and then chooses an action to engage the monsters.

And it works so-so, but Pandemic this isn't. If you liked Pandemic you won't like this. If you didn't like Pandemic you might like this. If you liked Arkham Horror, then you need your head adjusting and I don't care if you like this.

My dislike of Arkham aside that is the problem with this. It feels and plays like Pandemic, but you roll lots of dice at different points to determine if things work and so it feels very random.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I tend not to enjoy most co-ops in general - but this is better than most, and with some pretty nice components. By all accounts, though (and supported by my few plays), this is insanely hard. But too hard is better than too easy. I can't say I found it particularly fun, but this is definitely more interesting than Pandemic or Forbidden Island, and I would like to play it again at some point.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.7
Rocko Says: The best co-op game I have played yet!

I gave this a 9.7, it is so close to a 10... except for a few teeny tiny things.

Ghost Stories is the best co-op game I have played. It is a shorter game than Arkham Horror, which is great, less complicated than Arkham, and still more complicated than most modern board games :)

This game is So much fun! I cannot wait to play it with more people. I expect to play it many, many times over the next few years. 

The compononets and pieces are amazing. Next to Arkham, it is just the most beautiful game we have purchased yet.

What I liked:
1) The game is very well made. High quality, the highest.

2) The mechanics are like most co-op games: constant and worsening damage control. However, based on player decisions and strategies, there are a lot of options on how to deal with the damage. Sometimes the players can even out-pace the board and get ahead, which is rare in co-ops. 

The mechanics are also very interesting and have nuances that set Ghost Stories apart from other co-ops.

3) The artwork and story/theme are just the most groovy ever.

4) The gameplay is fun, unpredictable, and often thrilling. We get so excited playing this. When you lose- you really feel like youve been defeated. When you win- you feel on top of the world!

5) Playable by 2, 3 or 4. Even solo if you want. Lots of options.

6) Ghost Stories almost completely avoids co-op "quater-backing" (where players tell each other what to do- especially experienced players). Each player can make up their own mind and dont Have To spend 20 minutes planning ahead. We have a 'no quaterbacking' house rule for co-op games- it makes them more fun, I promise you.

7) After the first or second game, playtime can be under an hour if you setup fast.

8) lots of expansion options and house rule variants.

My only issues with the game:
1) The rules are difficult to understand at first. Once at least one person knows how to play, they can teach the others pretty quickly. I suggest: someone posted video tutorial on BBG, these taught me the game SUPER FAST! Watch these and then play it like 2 times, then you can show others how to play right away without reading or explaining all the rules- just jump right into it.

2) The 2-player variant is not as much fun as the 4 player game. The use of the extra 2 player boards is janky and not so accessible- I suggest that for 2 players, play a 4 player game instead, with each player controlling 2 character boards. That is a lot more fun!

3) One of the village tiles, the Solider/guard house, is pretty much useless. It slows the game down, and more importantly- if you use it you basically just worsen a bad situation. I suggest a house rule making it into a different kind of tile! Possibilities are endless.

4) The yellow and red players are under-powered if they are the active players in a 2 player game. This game ALMOST needs a house-rule saying that either one or both of the players in a 2-player game MUST play green and/or blue. Yellow and red are good support in a 3 or 4 player game, but Green is your powerhouse and Blue is your get-things-done guy. They are needed in a 2-player game. (experienced players can probably ignore that, or do it as a handicap for expert level play).

These 4 little things aside, this is one of my favorite games ever made, and definitely my favorite co-op so far. Mindy and I have tried co-ops such as Arkham Horror, Red November, and Pandemic. Ghost Stories is better than those games.

RATING: 4
I think this game is best played solo with all 4 players -- one person pretending to be 4.  True multi-player is very prone to sock puppetry, and the printed solo version I find boring -- not having to manage the resource between different characters ruins the game for me.  This game is hard, but it's winnable -- it require very tight coordination and planning; you do not last long if you act like individuals..

However, the scoring system is meaningless for measuring losses.  Usually terrible play gives you a better losing score than when you were a hair away from victory.  Given the brutality and high loss rate, it's frustrating that the scoring doesn't give you a better sense of how you are improving.

RATING: 7
06-09-2014. Rated after 3 plays (2 solo). I hate solo games, but I suspect it could be that Ghost Stories is better as a solo-game than with other players. Solo I lost horribly, but playing the normal game with my GF was no tension and we won easily.

GS is a very abstract cooperative game too, which is not a style I typically enjoy, being heavy on theme. It's very elegant though! You play a character that can move just one step per turn on a 3x3 board of Tiles with special actions. The player boards of the different colors, with enemy ghost being played on the player boards depending on their color. You basically try to clean them up as quickly as possible with using dice and tokens. Fun game.. but not so thematic as I like my games. I liked Police Precinct better (another coop I played recently).

RATING: 7
I had had such high hopes for this game, but it was a big flop with me and my wife.  A lot more fiddly than Pandemic, it just wasn't fun.  I think the dice used for exorcising the ghosts hurts the game a lot. Coop games are all of about solving the puzzle together - randomness from the game through uncertain order of cities in Pandemic or monsters in Castle Panic or tiles in Forbidden Island make the game interesting, but randomness from my choosing to take a chance rolling dice or not saps out all the fun, boiling down all my figuring out the puzzle to whether I get a lucky roll or not.  Yeah, you can mitigate the luck factor, and that's where the real strategy is, but that doesn't make for a fun game.  I won't scream if my gaming group wants to play it, but I will always recommend Pandemic over Ghost Stories.

Update: I'm warming to this one.  I still feel like you're really at the mercy of the dice - I feel like you should get some token reward for when you fail to roll the colors you need.  But I see more the potential to ensure that you are always able to kill at least one ghost regardless of what you roll.

RATING: 7.25
This is a punishingly difficult co-op game with a puzzly feel to it as players try to determine the best course of action against increasingly more dire odds.  Ghosts are drawn from a deck (random except for the placement of the "boss"), which can allow for variance of difficulty depending on draw order, but it is fairly consistent in being quite challenging but possible to defeat.  There is a possibility that you do draw a seemingly insurmountable sequence of ghosts, or that bad dice rolls ruin your chances (this is the issue which bothers me most, if any), but I find that that sort of crushing defeat is in the spirit of this game, and that the short length and easy setup make this a good "Let's try again!" kind of co-op.

RATING: 2.5
My impression of Ghost Stories is that it's actually pretty boring. Also, it feels like a step backwards in the development of the Cooperative Game genre. It makes no attempt to fix what I believe is the biggest failing of most cooperative games (and perhaps, the entire genre):

It's solitaire. It's not even multiplayer solitaire... one person can just play the game all by themselves. All weekend at BGG.con people were loving the game and talking about how hard it was, but I'm not sure that "hard" should correlate to "chances it's impossible to win, whether you know it or not." Pandemic suffers from that as well - some games you can't possibly win, but you don't know that until after you play. But I had the distinct feeling all throughout my games of Ghost Stories that I would have rather just been playing Pandemic.

RATING: 5
Cooperative game that works best with 1, 2 or 4 players. Beautiful artwork that complements the theme perfectly. The game seemed a little repetitive and free of tension (tension is a must for co-op!) during the mid-game, but that was probably because we were playing on beginner. The iconography scared me initially, but it was very intuitive. The game flows well and quickly, and the design is refreshing (ghosts entering the board via the player boards to haunt the village in the middle). Still, the playing time seems a tad too long (bring the boss out already!). We didn't discuss our moves too much, yet the game took nearly 90 minutes on beginner. In that sense, the design isn't as tight as Pandemic.

RATING: 8
A  brilliant "gamer's" game. One of the best solitaire game I own, in terms of its set-up time, play-time, and challenge.  I consistently play under "Normal" difficulty and win 1 out of every 6 games.  Tough.  And you definitely get the sense that your decisions matter.  There is much dice-rolling, but in a good way - you can tip the odds in your favor with good choices, and a bad roll forces you to adapt/adjust strategies on the fly.  Enormous variety in play-style from game-to-game, including how the board is set up, which powers each player has, the order in which ghosts arrive, and which incarnation is in the deck.  Wonderful, wonderful stuff.


Note:  the iOS version is quite good, although there's a lot packed into a tiny screen and you lose a lot of the ambiance and aesthetic character of the board version.

February, 2014:  traded this for Alien Frontiers

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Players are playing cooperatively and are Ghost Hunters trying to exorcise a variety of spirits, ghosts, monsters etc threatening to engulf a village. Each turn, ghost/s appear and players can move and exorcise a ghost or activate a special action on one of nine village tiles.

The object is to beat enough ghosts to get to the 'boss' ghost. Beat the 'boss' and players win!

Pluses: Gorgeous artwork and components.

Minuses: The ghosts felt too 'samey' and it felt like they purposely tweaked the game to make it hard for the sake of replayability and also because Pandemic was 'easier'. The movement and board felt too small and there weren't really that many 'meaningful' choice to make each turn. Move, exorcise or do a card action. It is more compact and tighter than Pandemic or Shadows.

And I really am not a huge fan of symbols to make a game multilingual. 

However, I do still want to play it if only to say I 'beat' the game. So that's a good sign.

RATING: 10
Ghost Stories is extremely gratifying in its challenge and gorgeous to boot. Right now it is my favorite co-op. 

One downside is the excessive use of symbols. They take some time to get used to. I printed and cut labels for the names and rules of the different village tiles, and that really helped to cut down on that time.

Also, if you're going at it with just two players, I recommend taking two boards each instead of dealing with power tokens.

RATING: N/A
The game is fun if you like cooperatives.  If you don't like them then obviously avoid this game.  It has die rolling and drawing from a deck that both add a luck factor to the game.  It is suspect to a leader taking over the game.  But all of that is basically always synonymous with this type of game.

For everyone else who can enjoy cooperatives, it has some of the best tension out of all these types of games I have played.  On the hardest difficulty you will almost always be barely holding off the board.  You can also reduce the luck factor in the game to a degree depending on how your group decides to play.

RATING: 3
Very abstract game: you got nine tiles and ghosts popping up every time. You can choose from several actions, but the one you actually resolve is either obvious or - since this is a coop game - suggested to you. Which is boring.

It also got what most eurogamers misconceive as theme: highly stylized components. However, the game tells absolutely no narrative, it's really just random ghosts popping up. The characters with their different abilities aren't elaborated either.

I don't mind the dice rolling/combat mechanism though, that's pretty neat.

Still, I have no desire to ever play this game again.

An absolute winner. I don't even know how mr Bauza could have designed such a well balanced game, and yet included such variety. I mean, you have all the great mechanics of the game and high tension throughout, but the 4 player characters all have different powers that all work together, and none of them supercede the others. RATING: 6
An interesting cooperative game. The game is generally hard - as you might have seen from some reviews. While I don't have much to say about it, the game production overall is very high. The pieces look great and as well as the overall design of the boards and cards.

In terms of game play, I found the concept interesting at first but after learning to play a game without accidentally breaking any rules, the game does not seem that interesting. You are pretty much killing the same enemies over and over until you kill the bosses. While I admit most other board games do the exact same thing, it does seem very annoying waiting for the reincarnations to "pop up".

The best part of the game? I would say the dice (I have a thing for good looking dice) as well as the rush to quickly kill all of the enemies off your board as they begin to accumulate across the game.

RATING: 6

So, it is not my favorite co-op (which of course could change some day) since I don't quite get the "ooh, need to try that again"-feeling from it but am willing to play occasionally. But, and this has to be said again, it is absolutely gorgeously looking.

RATING: 9
Ghost Stories seems to be a love it or hate it game - I'm one of those who loves it. The artwork is superb, and the components, particularly the Buddha figures, are outstanding, so a very big thumbs up for the physical quality.

The Introductory level was challenging for the first few games, but once I'd beaten that I could beat the Standard level as well. Ten games in I was playing at Nightmare level, and moved on to Hell level after twenty or so.

I played my first games solo so I would be able to teach it to others, and was rapidly addicted. In fact, I actually prefer solo play at this point. How best to exploit the power tokens is an interesting decision which is lost in a four player game, and I'm happy pursuing my own strategy without having to explain or negotiate.

The rules are not nearly as bad as some people claim, and help is readily available in the Rules Forum. When looking for specific rulings, I recommend a forum search with folder set to "Rules" and user set to "toinito" (the designer).

RATING: 6.5
[Repos 2008 edition] {Horror; co-operative, dice-rolling, variable-player-power; scalable}  Ghost Stories is a nicely produce games.  The plastic figures and the illustration of cards and tokens are attractive.  It is worth the price with this production quality.

Ghost Stories is not a ground-breaking co-operative games - players have to turn over cards for the 'devil' and to solve some mini-puzzles.  Nonetheless, it works well as a co-op game.  Players really need to work, play and communicate together in order to win.

Ghost Stories has several minuses.  Firstly, it is repetitive because each move is similar.  It is also anti-climax.  There is little excitement when the Wu-Feng incarnation appears and it is usually easy to kill the incarnation at the initiation game once it appears.  The game just ends so suddenly (I have similar feeling with Pandemic).  I think only the normal / nightmare will bring enough challenges for experienced players.  And, the cards are too random - some ghosts are just much more powerful / scary than others.  I also found that the game is not balanced with the arrangement of the 9 village tiles; some arrangements are more beneficial for the players.  The rulebook is a messy! I think they should really rewrite the whole thing and post a revised copy at their web site.  Finally, the theme, Chinese ghost stories, is novel but the system doesn't tie with the theme seamlessly.

There is certainly large dose of luck in Ghost Stories but I am not annoyed.  The luck really makes this game fun for me. 

I still can't make up my mind whether to purchase a copy or not.  It's not highly fun for me but the theme and components are attractive enough.  So far, after trying it, I am not as eager to buy it as before.  Maybe, I will get a copy when I have a larger house.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I'd been slavering over Ghost Stories since reading the hype about it from Essen, and I bought it on an impulse when on a vacation in Seattle. Reading over the rules later in the hotel room, I started to feel a bit trepidatious; they were a bit confusingly written with some questionable translation, and overall the concept of the game seemed a bit too repetitive and simple to be fun. I know that a simple concept doesn't necessarily mean that a co-op game can't kick your butt (see Pandemic), but, anyway, I was starting to worry that I'd blown $50 and valuable suitcase space (we never check luggage, so this is always at a premium on vacation) on an overhyped release with nice production values. After about half of a game that I abandoned, I was even more worried, but still determined to give the game a fair shake.

Oh wow, am I glad I did. When played with four people, this is an unmerciful, immersive, and downright fantastic co-op. It can suffer from the "loudest player" problem that a lot of open-info co-ops do, but, honestly, I find that to be largely unavoidable in many co-ops. It's somewhat mitigated by the fact that, usually, EVERYTHING is going wrong, and so there's often several answers for a given turn, none of which are particularly clearly correct. Ghost Stories is now one of my favorite co-operative games, often inspiring "just one more try" when we've gotten our butts handed to us, which is high praise for a game that tends to run about 45-60 minutes (usually once in a row is enough for an hour-length game for my group and me).

RATING: 9
It has exceeded my expectations. I love the way the game develops the tension as each ghost played brings something different to handle, and the complex interactions of the player powers and the village powers. I am usually wary of games with dice in, because of the potential for extreme turn-arounds based purely on chance, but in this game their effect is really well balanced. They add tension and excitement like dice should do, but don't dominate the game play. They are nicely balanced with the powers and the tao tokens. 

Also as a coop or solo game you can just write off a loss due to a run of bad throws as the luck of the dice, you don't have an opponent to worry about offending (by saying they were just lucky to win). 90 minutes is not too heavy an investment to then lose on bad luck, especially as you've had so much fun on the way.

The artwork is great, and the feel is great. I cannot wait for my next game.

RATING: 10
My first modern board game. Rules explanation can get a bit long, but once you get playing ...

The theme feels fun and fantastic. It's just silly enough to allow us to step back when the intensity rises too high and laugh at how screwed we are. And boy does the intensity rise quickly. This game strikes early and doesn't hold back. The first time the Ghosts line up into an impossibly perfect stream of deadly combos you will think it's a fluke. The next several times it happens you will come to the realization that Wu Feng is sentient, he is trapped in your board game, and he wants to destroy you.

Art and components are top quality. The rules are a bit muddy at points but the wonderful iconography allows me to forgive this.

The game is very difficult. But it never really feels like any one player's fault so the frequency at which we lose never becomes abrasive. Every turn becomes a puzzle, a tactical nightmare at the mercy of dice that will always be stacked against you and ghosts that should have been dead three turns ago laughing over the ruins of the innocent village you are failing miserably to defend. And I wouldn't have it any other way.

RATING: 8
Played many games on the Ipad, with no wins. 

Played twice with the boardgame. One was a crushing defeat. The other was an easy victory. Seems we were quite lucky on the order of the draw deck.

But the games offers tough decisions. You will need to do 3 or 4 things on your turn, but can only do one. Choosing where to place the ghosts requires some thinking.

Do you take a chance and try to exorcise the ghost only with the dice, or do you use tokens? Maybe the yellow player could help with that if he has the right power. Do you go for the though ghost that makes you roll the curse dice every turn, or the weak ghost that will haunt a tile in two turns?

Lots to think about, and requires a lot of teamwork between the monks to be successful. The different powers will mostly mean that each players will have a different role in the game, but sometimes you will be in the wrong place at the wrong time and you will have to take matters into your own hands.

The game provides lots of tension most of the time, barely holding the ghosts back and watching your qi slowly trickling away while you wait for Wu Fend to appear.

The game can offer brutal reversal. You'll have a few easy turns, controling the ghosts with no problems, then you'll get flooded with hard to kill nasty ghosts and monks will drop like flies. 

The tension in the game is dependant on the order in which the ghosts appears, but it is quite uncommon to have an easy game with no tension. Only happened to me once in 25 games.

RATING: 8.3

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.2
[i]Word of warning: We have not taken to cooperative gaming.[/i]

I LOVE the theme. Players team up to fight ghost, ghouls and other assorted bad boys. They try to stay ahead of the curve, but are often fighting a losing battle against the constant flow of evil encroaching on the town.

The game oozes theme and you feel a sense of accomplishment when you ultimately defeat the BIG baddie at the end. It is no mean feat and increasing the difficulty will keep you on your toes.

In your fight against evil you can call upon your very own special abilities, as well as those of the many inhabitants of the town, who are all willing to help you - after all, it is their small town in danger of being overrun.

The game will play out differently each time as the game board is set up using the tiles available, but mixed together. Sometimes you will have a great combo next to each other, sometimes they will be across town. It is also of importance in what order evil comes at you. You can get lucky and have a few easy pickings, helping you set up for the hard hitters, or you can be overwhelmed from the start.

It involves dice, so there is a random element here too, but nothing that should deter anyone from playing. This aspect can be mitigated to an extent by Tao tokens.

I enjoy the theme immensely, my wife less so. The game is fun and tense at the same time. It is a game that plays equally well solo as 2 player. The reason for this is perhaps that I tend to take charge, though not always with the proper course of action.

Our objections are very few, but they are significant. As I began stating, we have not really taken to the whole cooperative gaming aspect. It is fun for a while, but it just doesn't hold the lasting appeal for us - even with a killer theme.

You get lucky breaks from time to time, but most of the time you feel you are running around putting out fires. I think we prefer a more slow paced game. This game is meant to be played with monsters coming at you from all sides...

My rating reflects these "grievances". At the end of the day I would be more than happy to play a game of [gameid=37046] but I see no need to own it, nor seek it out.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Ghost Stories is heralded as one of the toughest cooperative games you can buy.  Playing up to 4 players, you take on the roles of nameless defenders of a village being overrun by denizens of the undead.  Using your own skills and the skills of the villagers in town, in coordination with the other players, is key to landing a victory in this game.   

The art in this game is excellent.  The ghosts are all creatively designed, and the primary + green colors all integrate with a black backdrop that is wonderful to look at. 

This game after the first turn always feels down to the wire.  There will be a lot of group effort to determine the most efficient play possible.  It is painful to see something go wrong because the ghosts can snowball out of control in a hurry, leaving you with dead monks and a haunted village.

I personally love the difficulty in this game, but it is a HARD game to introduce new players to correctly.  Letting other people experience the game for the first time without commanding the most efficient course of action from them (aka being an alpha gamer) is hard to balance without coming off as disingenuous.  If you can play this with people who have played about as often as you, then you are in for a treat.  

So why is this is a 7?  Well, simply put, I feel I have solved this game, so the replay-ability has run its course for me.  I love introducing new people to this game, but I don't like dominating the game decisions OR holding back and watching mistakes get made.  I wholeheartedly recommend this game as a fun, intensely challenging, coordinative experience.  As long as I'm not playing ;)

Watch out for this one, it's hard, even with only a single Incarnation of Wu-Feng to face - players must take advantage of every action they can, while fighting a set of dice that seem to be against them at every roll.

RATING: 4
At first, I really liked this game. The high difficulty and interesting theme caught my attention. I was also fresh off of Pandemic, which was very fun. But the more I played Ghost Stories, the less I liked it. So much comes down to the random order of the ghost cards, and of the dice rolls. You can use the different board elements to stem the tide, but most of the time you can see your defeat coming many turns out. Too much luck and too little chance of winning make this an incredibly frustrating experience (in a bad way).

UPDATE: I employed the help of a Ghost Stories expert to show me the way. And we won. Hurray! I did learn that I had misinterpreted one rule -- a minor difference. For now, however, I am only raising my rating from a 2 to a 3. I've learned that I like the luck in cooperative games to define the challenge (e.g., card flipping in Pandemic), and not whether I can beat the challenge (e.g., rolling dice in Ghost Stories). I *am* happy to know that the game can in fact be won.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.7
There is no room for wasted moves in this fast paced co-op. The invading ghosts won't hold up, and every turn, every action needs to not only contain their numbers but also forward plan for more dangerous threats. Cleaning up messes won't be enough. I thoroughly enjoy the difficulty of this game. It works well as a solo game (as it is heavily prone to alpha gaming) and I prefer to play as all four players rather than the suggested solo mode. Winning will feel so sweet, as you will need to work hard - there is some luck involved, but a lot of strategy is needed; knowing when to respond to threats and when to let them go in order to plan ahead. The theme works well with the fast-paced action and the abilities of the characters are interesting and quite variable. There is not much variation however in the miniatures, but still, the game still looks quite stunning.

RATING: 8
Probably my favorite co-op after Pandemic, because I'm masochist. I've only experienced one win, and that was playing with other people who knew what they were doing. This one is HARD. Even on the beginner level. It takes a bit getting used to, as well, to remember all of the powers and iconography. However, the game is very immersive once you give it a chance, and tons of fun. Make sure you learn this from someone else or use a BBG rules book because the one that comes with the game is terrible. The worst I've ever seen, actually. The cards are a little rough, too, so you might sleeve them if that's your thing. I also had an issue with sticky dice, but Asmodee replaced them without much fanfare. It's a great game, though, with a great theme. I highly recommend it.

RATING: 8
A terrific cooperative game that does what so many others fail to do ... it pressures players to play well or fail and, more importantly, gives players the opportunity to make clever moves. The theme is engaging and a hard-fought win very satisfying. Ranks with Pandemic and Battlestar Galactica in the upper echelons of cooperative games. With the advent of this new breed of cooperative, I can't picture myself playing Shadowns Over Camelot or Lord of the Rings much in the future.

RATING: 6
First Impression:

A tough cooperative game, with elegant mechanics and a superb pace.

The game manages to be tough without having the players feel weak or helpless and almost without luck. The pace of the game is also great, as the players easily manage the situation at the early game, and then ever so gradually become overwhelmed. The gameplay is very easy yet it forces some very tough decisions, and cooperation between the monks is essential for victory. Finally the game is pretty and the theme caries through very very well.

As with all classic cooperative games, Ghost Stories also potentially suffers from the Alpha Player syndrome, even if the tough decisions create many opportunities for disagreements. The village tiles are not of equal strength, and we found ourselves prefering the same old most of the time, even though some are extremelly important if all hell breaks lose.

Overall this is very well polished game, and as a fan of cooperative games I enjoy it very much.
