RATING: 9
Ghost Stories is the best cooperative game I've ever played and it's a very crowded field these days, what with the recent release of Pandemic, Red November, Space Alert, and the semi-cooperative Battlestar Galactica, all being added to the previous bulwarks of the genre Lord of the Rings and Shadows over Camelot. Cooperative games have come a long way in recent years as more of them are published and designers experiment with a wider variety of elements in creating their cooperative designs. I'm sure cooperative games still have a long way to go in their development with many more innovations and twists, but for the time being, I am more than satisfied with Ghost Stories. I've played it 23 times already since its release last October and have enjoyed every play, even those in which my fellow Taoist priests and I have been mercilessly crushed by Wu-Feng and his minions. Ghost Stories is renowned for its difficulty, which has been off-putting to some, but as someone who prizes the challenge of Survival Games such as Antiquity, Age of Steam, and La Citta, the extreme difficulty of Ghost Stories is one of its merits, not one of its flaws. I appreciate the challenging nature of Ghost Stories and other Survival Games because it rewards repeated plays. It rewards revisiting the game time and again despite repeated failure in order to learn where you went wrong and what you can improve upon next time. You might go bankrupt in Age of Steam or drown in pollution and graves in Antiquity, but if you keep at it, you'll learn to conquer those obstacles. The same goes for Ghost Stories where you'll eventually find yourself breezing through the game after many failed attempts. You might think this would mean you would never want to play the game again, but fortunately the game has 4 difficulty settings, ranging from Initiation, to Normal, Nightamre, and finally Hell. It's amusing to see people's reaction when you tell them after they've lost horribly that they were playing on the Initiation difficulty level. Just as with Pandemic, the inclusion of a variety of difficulty levels is a very wise move in any cooperative game since it allows players to adjust the challenge based on the experience of the players.

I'd be remiss if I didn't mention another significant advantage of Ghost Stories, which is the way it wonderfully scales to accomodate 1 to 4 players. All of the player counts work remarkably well, and as someone who's picky about that sort of thing, I greatly appreciate a rare gem like Ghost Stories that can work with many different size groups. I should also mention the Guardhouse mini-expansion for Ghost Stories, which I think adds a nice element of variety to the experience. Unlike most mini-expansions, which either add nothing meaningful to the game (e.g., Ticket to Ride Mystery Train or Settlers of Catan Fisherman) or actively harm the game (e.g., Saint Petersburg Banquet), the Guardhouse mini-expansion for Ghost Stories is the first of its kind that I've found to actually improve the game. It adds a tenth village tile to the game, which increases the variety of the board layout as you remove a random village tile from each game, and also adds five new cards to the deck of ghost cards (similarly with five random cards removed). Most importantly, the new tile and cards fit seamlessly into the mechanics and theme of the game. This gives me great hope for the upcoming White Moon full expansion for the game, previously announced on Boardgame News.

Ghost Stories is my favorite game of 2008 (http://games.fooville.net/#Award2008) for all of the reasons explained above but most importantly because of the mood and feeling of the game, which are difficult to put into words. Ghost Stories is a game in which the players represent Taoist priests defending a village from invading ghosts. The ghosts are attacking from all sides. The village and the players are surrounded. You feel this when you're playing. You feel trapped and surrounded. You feel like you're running from place to place putting out fires and addressing the most urgent emergency. The assault of ghosts is relentless and you feel the relentless attack as the ghosts keep coming, filling in the places vacated by the previous ghost that you just defeated. It reminds me of the scene in Song of Ice and Fire where the Night's Watch is surrounded and attacked on the Fist of First Men. The reference may not mean anything to many of you (in which case I recommend reading George R.R. Martin's Song of Ice and Fire series), but in that case the game may remind you of a scene in a different movie or book where the characters were surrounded and outnumbered by a relentless foe. This game is an uphill battle. You're faced with a Sisyphean challenge. It's incredibly difficult, but that makes victory all the sweeter.

Received as gift: Christmas 2008

RATING: 7
My first coop game. Maybe my last, but not because I dislike this particular game. I'm just mostly interested in 3+ player games.

Anyway, I had fun. My monks all got killed, but I lasted surprisingly long from the moment I realized I was in trouble. Difficult decisions regarding which fires to put out first.

So, the game seems quite difficult, but I wondered if it would be "too" difficult. It occurs to me now that it might not even matter if the game was so hard that it could never be won, because you could at least try to top your best attempt.

I also worried about people saying this game is abstract. I didn't like the sound of that but was also unsure what would be bad about it. As it turns out I didn't think the game was too abstract: There are enough things that make thematic sense that a sensible narrative can form in my mind as I'm playing. And that must be it: Purely abstract games don't easily tell a relatable story.

...Played a bit with the family (it is a real hit) recently and won a couple of times. Winning can be pretty anticlimactic. Losing too, though. I felt the abstract nature of it more when trying to explain the game to the 3-year-old who wanted to be part of it. There's no good way to explain what the player boards and colors represent. A green ghost threatens the green monk and attacks from his specific cardinal direction... What's it mean? So you can't use the theme to help answer rules questions, magnifying the unhelpfulness of the rules booklet.

RATING: 6
For somewhat unknown reasons, my wife likes this more than I do (we play 2-player, each controlling 2 Taoists).  

I can say that I feel games are too similar from one to the next, despite the variation brought in by 2 different special abilities for each Taoist, randomization of when ghosts come in, and the variety of boss cards.  

I do enjoy the game but.. I just don't feel like I "need" to play it.  It's challenging, which I enjoy,  but it feels a little too programmed to me.  In other words, I feel like the 'best' action is always the 'best' action, and so once you've identified which action you can take, it doesn't change much.

With all of this said, I've only beaten the game on normal (not the two higher difficulties).  I don't think I would enjoy it more on those difficulties, though.

RATING: 7.5
Played seven times with 2 and 4 and absolutely loved it. The free Essen '08 giveaway (a village tile and some additional ghosts) seems a worthwile little expansion. The game is quite easy to grasp if explained to you, but the manual takes a little bit of getting used to and is structured in an unintuitive way. Moreover, the German rules are definitely a bit clearer than the English ones. The whole package, however, is awesome - artwork is impressive, theme is appealing and well implemented and turns are fast. Cannot wait to play again! My only concerns are that the game seems to be much harder to win with two than it would be with four, and that it has (and I hate to say this) limited replayability. But only time will tell...
UPDATE: Played it more and have grown to like it more, although the game (in general) is a little bit too hard to beat. After 12 games, we finally managed to win a single game on normal level! Still, everybody I introduced it to wanted to give it a try because of the theme and its great looks. Surely a a good addition to my collection, although I still like Pandemic a l i t t l e bit better. In general, however, I am not a big fan of co-op games, since the replayability of this type of game always seems a bit limited.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
A hit with the boys.

I read a few of the low rated comments to get a feel why some people don't like this game. "Yatzhee I killed a ghost." "The die won the game." "No real decisions." "Too hard." "Frustrating when its hard to move and then fail on a dice roll." They are playing it wrong. The dice are just for "saving tokens". 

This is resource management co-op. If you take on ghost without the corresponding tao-token, luck is your only hope. Share tokens (stand in the same spot as another taoist when exorcising) and stock up on token all the time. 

My kids and I love playing this game. The dice add suspense, but don't make or break a game if you play with the right strategy. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

2009-09-11 - Increased score to 5.  Game is growing on me slightly, but I still tend to enjoy other co-ops more.

RATING: 7
Flew under my radar as another co-op game, this time with a theme that I don't care for (horror).  Well, turns out that the title of the game doesn't really do its theme justice.  I thought I would get cheap slasher horror theme, and we open up this game and it's set... in China?  In [i]feudal[/i] China?  With artwork that's at least as much fantasy as horror?  Sign me up!  The presentation is really gorgeous.  The art is dark and beautiful, and the pieces appropriately looming and dynamic.  The components are backed up by an interesting and tense ruleset.  There's randomness and risk-taking that really keeps things interesting.  If you like co-ops, at least give this one a look, and consider buying.  This is the best pure cooperative game since [gameid=823].

RATING: 9
PERMANENT PLACE IN COLLECTION

A brilliant cooperative game that's unbelievably hard. It will drive you insane, you will die... You will vow to do better next time, play again, die...

After about 30 sessions, you may narrowly win. Before promptly losing again.

The pieces are gorgeous and the gameplay is novel. The rulebook sucks though, but Boardgamegeek and various other websites have lots of advice on how to play.

We've played two player, and that works well. Recommended without hesitation to anyone who doesn't mind losing repeatedly to a board.

Replay value is good, but you get burned out after a while.

Many fell putting an end to the reign of terror of Wu-Feng, Lord of the Nine Hells. The funerary urn housing his ashes was buried in the cemetery of a village in the Middle Empire.
\13\\13\
Years have passed, and the cursed legacy has been forgotten by the living. Hidden away in Hell, Wu-Feng has forgotten nothing. His incessant research allowed him to locate the receptacle. The shadow of his former incarnation already extends to the villagers, who are unaware of the danger threatening them.
\13\\13\
Fortunately, the Fat-Si (Taoist priests) keep watch, guarding the border between the dead and the living. Armed with their courage, their faith, and their powers, they will try to return the reincarnation of Wu-Feng to Hell.
\13\\13\
Ghost Stories is a cooperative game. The players play as a team against the game. Either they share a common victory, or suffer the same defeat. Ghost Stories provides 4 levels of difficulty: Initiation, Normal, Nightmare, and Hell.

RATING: 5
This game is hard. Mind you, my Pandemic record is something like 1-8, so I'm not the best coop gamer, but I'll still play Pandemic because, after the game, I can usually look back and think "OK, we shouldn't have done that" and the game was close enough that it makes me want to try again. This game is so hard that I don't even want to try to get better at it. It wasn't fun to just continually get pummeled, and I don't know what we could've done differently that would've bought us more than maybe a couple of turns. The only way I'd want to play this again would be with a person who has won before (so I can understand it better) or if I find out we got a rule wrong (in which case, I'll withdraw my rating). I'm not crazy about fully cooperative games in general, and this wasn't my least favorite of them (that would be Red November), so take that into consideration. I'm sure people who routinely beat Pandemic on the highest difficulty would enjoy this, as there are some interesting design things going on here (which is why I rate it as highly as I do). It just was not fun for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Ghost Stories is a chillingly tense (and difficult) game and is, in my experience, perfectly executed.  Ghost Stories is a co-op that accomodates from 1 to 4 players and honestly plays just as well with any of those player counts.

The players feel constantly overwhelmed (albeit, excitedly so) during the game.  Everytime they seem like they're breaking even, another obstacle rears its ugly head and has the players scrambling to deal with it.

Although the onslaught against the players is relentless, they will find that they have so many options and strategies available to them and, carefully managed, those strategies can lead to fantastic, white-knuckle victories.

This is one of the most exciting, challenging and outright fun games I've ever played.  The components are gorgeously produced, the game is completely tight and streamlined and the gameplay has an incredible arc, with a slow build-up in the initial rounds, culminating in a furious and nail-biting climax.

A supreme example of how to create an engaging and challenging cooperative game.

RATING: 7
Ghost Stories is a quality production, although it does share certain characteristics with other cooperative games.

In terms of GS's qualities of "sameness", the game includes unique player abilities, a constant barrage of danger and dread, multiple ways to lose, and a focus on killing an evil overlord. These same elements can be found (piecemeal) in Pandemic, Shadows over Camelot, Lord of the Rings, Vanished Planet, and Arkham Horror.

However, the theme in GS is neat, the game art is ferociously attractive, and GS does contribute a handful of newness to the cooperative game field: location-based special actions, dice-driven combat mitigated by power chits, an over-the-top difficulty level, and oddly-named minions of evil.

As noted elsewhere, though, all information in GS is completely open, which means that there’s a real possibility that a single experienced player can dominate the entire proceedings, which would be entirely unfun.

Finally, GS has proven that the general gaming community is willing to put up with an inordinate amount of die-rolling, as long as there are no actual numbers on the dice.  Colors and symbols on die faces are OK, I guess, but standard dice apparently leave a wargame/Ameritrash aftertaste.  Fair enough.  I’ve now learned a lesson about game marketability and design.

[i]Update[/i]:

After six years of off-and-on enjoyment, I'm not sure that my body can handle another ghost ulcer.  This game is just impossible to win (10% success rate?), even at the easiest level.  Anyone arguing otherwise is [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/filepage/121361/ghost-stories-official-big-faq]playing incorrectly[/url].

Still fun occasionally (Halloween), preferably with the "we take pity on you" White Moon expansion and a spooky soundtrack.

RATING: 9
One of the best cooperative games out there. The Asian ghost story theme is widely recognised and familiar in Singapore, adding to the enjoyment. The designer has obviously done his research, including well-known artifacts such as glutinous rice (wards off vampires!), Taoist mirrors, incense sticks, and talismans in the game. This has replaced Shadows over Camelot as the cooperative game of choice in my group. Works well with casual gamers too.

RATING: 6
(Trade Interest: low) i like the theme, and the degree to which you have to cooperate with the other players.  it has lots of interesting mechanics, and good graphics.  i think it is WAY too difficult, and though you can get better at it, i would not want to play very often unless the difficulty were adjusted down.  i mean, it's not fun to lose 90% of the time.  further thoughts on the game come with more plays: the cooperation aspect is too much group-think for there to be much fun.  Everyone has to agree and execute their moves perfectly, or it will result in a loss.  there is no individuality, and that makes the game not much fun, except as an exercise in four people making an agreement.  will never surpass Arkham Horror on the coop game front.

RATING: 7.5
Gorgeous artwork with a very familiar theme to me personally (I grew up watching Chinese ghost and zombie movies after all).  This was probably the one game I looked forward the most to trying out of Essen 2008.  Well, I'm sad to say that my first experience with it left me kind of disappointed.

Ghost Stories is far from easy.  Your situation can go from good to bad in the blink of an eye.  Every decision you make as a group will be meaningful, so there are never really any wasted actions.  Unfortunately, the mechanics of each turn felt very procedural: resolve the bad actions, draw a ghost card, perform a good action, rinse and repeat.  Now don't get me wrong, I know very well that strictly speaking all boardgames are just the same set of steps one take over and over again.  However, in Ghost Stories that just stuck out like a sore thumb to me.  While the tension is there, but I was never truly immersed in the play to make it seem less obvious.

I liked it ok, but certainly failed to be the definitive co-op title I was hoping for.

Update #1: Bumped the rating up by half a point.  Subsequent plays were a lot more enjoyable.  It's all about maximizing your actions and not to perform any risky ones that will net you nothing.  I've also taught it several times.  Ghost Stories is actually legitimately hard with tension, and I would say a much better game than Pandemic.

RATING: 10
This has to be in my top 3 list!  This game is close to perfect for my taste!

The game play is outstanding!  Every session is fun, challenging and rewarding... especially if you win as it can be really tough.  A lot of planning went into the production of this game and it is very apparent.

The game components are next to perfect.  Everything from the minatures to the game tiles, chits and cards are very high-quality and intricately detailed.  I would have to say that these components are more than worth the price of the game!   

The artwork is enticing!  Honestly, this game could win an award for best illustrations!  Not only does the artwork do an excellent job projecting the theme, but it is as alluring as the game play!  I am usually not very fond of comic books, anime, etc., but these illustrations really play into the theme flawlessly.

This has to be my favorite from Asmodée!

Ghost Stories, however, throws so much at you so hard and so fast and on such a small playfield, that it mitigates this problem. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
As a non-geek I was surprised by the style of the game: first that it's a coop game and than, after playing it for a couple of times and getting used to the difficult and numerous rules, the method; I have never played such a game before and I adored it.
However, for non-geeks it is an extremely hard game with rare feelings of success; so we invented the "luck dice", aided our decision with the philosophical notion: "yeah, life is hard, but not THAT much and sometimes you may be lucky!". 
It works like this: change one of the village cards for the blank one at start. You can use the luck dice as it's help; you may roll it only once. The dice is white with 6 sides, 2 of them is empty -- nothing happens; the rest 4 possibilities: turn back 1 haunted village, you can have your yin yang token back, you can destroy a ghost card (no curse, no reward), you can move the ghosts back on a gamer's card. We haven't tried it yet but I am sure it won't make the game much more easier; only a bit more life-like...
Summing the game: beautiful, exciting aaaand annoying – just like a fine woman. :)

说实话，游戏难度有点大，而且策略可控性较差，如开局运气稍差点的话，团灭是很正常的事情。IOS版更适合单人挑战，是款比较挑人的游戏。不知道加了一扩二扩的对抗模式后，耐玩性上是否有更大的提升。。。
